Su Provincial Government

Entire Committee Resigns 106

Due to Financial Difficulties, Nothing Can Be Done

Zhenjiang Dispatch: The entire committee of the Jiangsu Provincial Government has submitted a request to the Executive Yuan for resignation, due to financial difficulties and the inability to carry out any work. The original request is as follows: "We hereby submit this request due to the exhaustion of finances and the inability to proceed with various administrative matters. We earnestly request approval for our resignation in order to avoid delaying provincial affairs. We respectfully congratulate our colleagues for being appointed to preside over the administration of Jiangsu Province. Following the collapse of the Grand Canal and during the period when embankment work awaits repair, the provincial treasury was already very strained, and raising funds was especially difficult. However, considering the millions of disaster victims and the devastation in more than ten counties, we felt deeply distressed and could not rest day or night. Due to our responsibilities, we dared not refuse the difficulties. We exhausted the provincial treasury, borrowed from banks, and solicited from charitable organizations. The total funds raised amounted to slightly more than two million yuan. In addition, we were ordered to assist with one million yuan. This major project could be completed on schedule. However, only one hundred thousand yuan of the assistance funds has been allocated to date. Subsequently, the War of Resistance against Japan erupted, and large armies converged. Jiangsu Province bore the brunt of the impact. All kinds of rear-area needs, such as the recruitment of laborers, the requisition of ships, the procurement of materials, the supply of provisions, the treatment of wounded soldiers, the accommodation of displaced women and children, and the facilities for air defense, poison gas prevention, and the repair of city walls as ordered, all required huge sums of money and could not be delayed. We and our colleagues, mindful of the great righteousness of resisting Japan and aware of the fierceness of the war, instructed all counties to raise funds with great effort. These were all expenditures of the provincial treasury. Although we repeatedly petitioned the central government to handle military logistics, we have not yet received an order to implement it. In total, the funds advanced by various counties in Jiangsu Province for the War of Resistance amount to more than one million yuan. Last year, a major flood occurred, and the Jiangnan seawall was also impacted by storm tides, with many breaches. Coastal counties were severely affected. We were planning to cooperate with the Shanghai Municipal Government to plan repairs, but the War of Resistance broke out, making it impossible to proceed. Since the establishment of the ceasefire agreement, we have been earnestly planning and undertaking repairs. The funds required for temporary repairs are estimated at two million yuan, but only more than four hundred thousand yuan has been raised so far. Combining these temporary expenditures, they have reached four million yuan. Jiangsu Province is a rich area, and its finances have always been considered ample. However, since we and our colleagues took office, we have thoroughly audited the accumulated deficits over the years, which amount to a staggering twenty million yuan. In addition, due to last year's floods and this year's military affairs, land taxes have been sharply reduced, and there is no revenue from business taxes. Even without temporary expenditures, it would be impossible to maintain the status quo. Moreover, embankment work, seawall work, and military advances have added significantly to the burden, and they are all essential and cannot be delayed. The province's financial resources are limited. An increase in one area will inevitably lead to a shortage in another. Therefore, although provincial administrative expenses have been tightened again and again, and affiliated institutions have been merged again and again, we have also followed the clear orders of the central government to provide all civil servants in the province with living expenses, hoping to overcome this difficult time with a spirit of austerity.

However, military and police expenses, as well as administrative expenses, are still in arrears for five, six, three, or four months. Although we have tried to follow the precedent of seventeen years ago by requisitioning two months' rent from the entire province, hoping to provide some relief, the amount collected is very small due to various factors. It is like a drop in the bucket, which is of no help. Currently, the canal embankment is nearing completion, but still requires more than six hundred thousand yuan. The seawall work is just beginning, and the shortfall is also hundreds of thousands of yuan. The twentieth year is coming to an end, and the arrears of military, police, and administrative expenses are even greater. Looking ahead, our worries are endless. This is the real situation of the exhausted finances of Jiangsu Province in the twentieth year. For several months, we and our colleagues have lamented the financial difficulties of Jiangsu Province and the inability to carry out administrative affairs. We have repeatedly consulted, hoping to remedy the situation in the twenty-first year. Therefore, we ordered the Department of Finance to accurately audit the income and expenditure of various temporary funds and prepare a budget. However, after many discussions, the draft budget could not be established. The main sources of income for the provincial treasury are only land taxes and business taxes. More than a year has passed since the implementation of the business tax, but due to various practical difficulties, it not only fails to offset the likin tax, but also fails to cover the collection costs. It is realistically impossible to use it as a reliable source of funds. The total annual income from land taxes, excluding the designated education funds, which amount to more than two million yuan, is only more than five million yuan. Adding other miscellaneous income, the total is only more than seven million yuan. Moreover, it is necessary to repay bank loans for canal embankment and seawall work, military advances from various counties, and short-term loans from the twentieth year. The income that can be listed as provincial treasury revenue is only more than three million yuan. The lowest amount required for temporary expenses is more than fourteen million yuan, resulting in a shortfall of more than ten million yuan. Moreover, essential policies during the period of political tutelage, such as local autonomy, land surveying, and road policing, all require huge sums of money and urgently need to be implemented. However, given the current state of the provincial treasury, it is impossible to even maintain the status quo, let alone start construction. We have repeatedly consulted and tried to find ways to increase revenue from among the impossible, but either they are restricted by laws and regulations, or they hinder the central government's tax revenue. It seems inappropriate to interfere with the central government's prestige due to the difficulties of one province. Thinking day and night, we are at a loss. We and our colleagues were ordered to come to Jiangsu, originally hoping to do our best to promote political tutelage, to repay the expectations of the central government and to comfort the people's hopes. However, things have gone against our wishes, and our hearts are willing, but our strength is insufficient. Rather than holding on to our positions and wasting resources, both our own and the province's, it would be better to retire early to make way for the capable. After repeated discussions and consultations, we have unanimously decided to state the actual situation of the exhausted finances and the inability to promote administration. We humbly request approval for our resignation in order to avoid delaying matters. We are grateful beyond measure. Respectfully submitted to Wang, President of the Executive Yuan. Local dispatch."

Chamber of Commerce Relieves Unemployed Merchants: At the third joint meeting of the current session of the Jiangsu Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the representative of the Jinle District Chamber of Commerce proposed a motion to request local chambers of commerce to find ways to relieve unemployed merchants. Three measures were adopted: (1) The chamber of commerce should first conduct a survey of the number of unemployed people in the local area and conduct registration and review. (2) Those with bad habits and improper behavior should be sent to the local vagrant workshop to quit their habits and be forced to work. (3) A. Organize a job placement office. B. Organize an unemployment relief fund committee. C. Organize an interest-free loan office. In European and American countries, there are monthly statistics on the number of unemployed people, which is given extraordinary attention. Jiangsu Province has recently experienced natural disasters and man-made calamities, and all industries are in decline. The number of unemployed people is increasing daily. If no measures are taken to relieve them, they will inevitably face financial ruin, go astray, and affect social stability. Yesterday, the measures were copied and sent to local chambers of commerce for planning and implementation.

Construction Department Strictly Demands Construction Bond Loans: The Jiangsu Construction Department recently sent a telegram to the Wuxi County Government regarding the construction of the Jing-Tang Road, demanding that three thousand yuan be continuously transferred from the construction bond loan under the construction expenses item within five days, with severe punishment for exceeding the deadline. County Magistrate Chen, upon receiving the telegram, stated that although various funds had been collected and deposited in Wuxi, they had already been fully transferred and there were no remaining funds available for allocation. He submitted it to the 141st county administrative meeting for joint discussion. It was decided that the county had previously borrowed 30,000 yuan from various organizations for construction expenses due to urgent military needs to cope with the situation. Later, upon receiving the department's order to return the funds, the original borrowing organizations were consulted to find ways to raise funds and return them to the original depositing bank separately. Based on the department's check-signing, 16,000 yuan was disbursed for repair expenses and 6,000 yuan for military expenses. Of the remaining 8,000 yuan, 5,000 yuan had already been allocated for construction bond loans, leaving only 3,000 yuan. Since a telegram was received from the provincial government forwarding a telegram from the Military Commission, ordering the preparation of wages for the excavation of trenches from the Changshu border to Taihu Lake in the county, a total of seventy li in length, the amount was large and the deadline was tight, and the matter concerned national defense, it was not dared to delay. After much searching and scraping, it was still far from enough. It was unavoidable to temporarily divert these three thousand yuan to meet the emergency, and it was reported to the provincial government to allocate funds for reimbursement. Now that the deadline is imminent, it can only be reported for allocation after the wages for the trench construction are reimbursed by the provincial government. The section chief of the department, Lin Lizheng, was dispatched to the Construction Department to personally present the details of the incident. Director Dong severely rebuked Chen, saying that the county magistrate had failed to comply with the order to raise and disburse funds, and had made excuses to delay. He still demanded that the funds be raised and disbursed immediately.

Educational News and Important Information

Hunan Province Teachers and Staff 111

Celebrate Teachers' Day

Changsha Dispatch, June 6: The national education sector has designated June 6 as Teachers' Day. Hunan teachers and staff Yu Zhenchu, Fang Kegang, Luo Jiaoduo, and others, due to the fact that teachers and staff opinions in Hunan have been scattered in recent years, making it difficult to reach a consensus on any proposition, held the first Teachers' Day celebration in Changsha at Zhongshan Hall at 2 PM this afternoon for the sake of their fellow teachers and to improve teachers' treatment and enhance their self-cultivation. More than 300 people attended. Wen Yawen presided over the meeting, explaining the significance of holding Teachers' Day and the points that should be worked on in the future. Then Chen Shuyuan of the Party Committee and Xie Kun, a representative of the student union, spoke in succession, hoping to guide young students based on the actual situation and objective experience and to determine an education plan to shed a ray of light on the education sector in southern Hunan. Subsequently, many people gave free speeches. Finally, after mutual discussion, the following resolutions were made: (1) Submit a request to the Education Department to forward to the Ministry of Education to confirm June 6 as Teachers' Day, and to close schools for one day on that day for commemoration. (2) Send telegrams to educational institutions inside and outside the province to unanimously endorse the three points advocated by the education sector in Beijing and Shanghai: improving teachers' treatment, guaranteeing teachers' status, and enhancing teachers' self-cultivation. (3) Issue a declaration. (4) Submit a request to the Provincial Party Headquarters for permission to organize a joint association of teachers and staff, and nominate Wen Yawen, Zeng Shengzhai, Wang Tingkai, Yu Shenchu, Yang Bairong, Huang Dean, Pan Shimo, and others as temporary preparatory members. (5) The Provincial Education Association should be established within a limited time. (6) Assist teachers and staff in Hengyang and Changde in requesting the issuance of back pay to maintain their livelihoods, and appoint seven temporary preparatory members to be responsible for negotiating with the Education Department. (7) Teachers and staff salaries are meager; submit a request to the government to exempt them from discounts. (8) Send a telegram to support the Shanghai All-Circles Alliance to Abolish Civil War. (9) Determine a plan to improve teachers' treatment, enhance teachers' self-cultivation, and guarantee teachers' status, and adopt it as amended.

Commissioner Zhou Fo-hai of the Jiangsu Provincial Education Department's Letter to Teachers and Staff in Jiangsu Province (II) 112

I have always believed that the greatest task of education has three aspects: cultivating personality, guiding thought, and imparting knowledge. Therefore, all three must be present in order to complete the entire task of education. It has been more than thirty years since our country began to establish schools. Speaking of its effectiveness, the people's intelligence has been developed day by day, the people's morality has been followed day by day, thoughts have become increasingly mixed, and the academic atmosphere has become increasingly frivolous. The collapse has flowed horizontally, and its momentum has been unstoppable. Where is the benefit that the country and society have received from the school? It is difficult for anyone to point it out. Exhausting decades of time and exhausting the efforts of people across the country, the harvest is actually like this. What is more painful than this? Although it is said that the evolution of facts and the causes are multiple, the fact that educators only focus on the infusion of knowledge and neglect the guidance of personality and thought is the main cause of this evil result. The scale of modern schools is vast, and the number of students is also large. Educators regard enlightening knowledge as their primary responsibility, and scholars regard acquiring knowledge as their satisfaction. The function of the school has become merely a place for knowledge vendors. The personality and thoughts of thousands of people are entrusted to the hands of two or three fostering personnel. What about the words and actions of students? What about the progress of students? How can they increase their healthy personality? How can they point out their correct thoughts? It is a matter of asking the teacher and the scholar. Moreover, they regard the position of the teacher as equal to the labor of the contract, and the sacred altar as equal to the factory of employment. There is no emotional connection between the teacher and the disciple, and the disciples treat the teacher as if they were just passers-by who happened to meet. Honesty and sincerity are not in accord on weekdays, so once a dispute arises, there is no way to eliminate it beforehand, and there is even more loss of control and guidance after the incident. Even between teachers and students, they form a confrontation, as if they were enemies. This is why the academic atmosphere is deteriorating day by day. The good and bad seedlings are left to grow on their own, so only the best talents can know themselves, strive hard, and establish themselves in a prominent way. Those of medium qualifications, once entering society, are like raw silk dyed black, and they are increasingly dark and rarely able to extricate themselves. The most cunning of them will also use their acquired intelligence as a weapon to do evil and sell favors. In this case, how can we receive the effect of education? Moreover, there are occasionally a few unscrupulous people who want to achieve their private plunder and do not hesitate to use students as a tool for their horizontal and vertical expansion, so that pure young people are daily accustomed to the conspiracy of infighting and hooking doors, and become their mechanical and treacherous evil virtues. The decline of the teacher's way has actually reached this point, then what else can we say? I have been lecturing in various schools in recent years, and I have seen these phenomena and secretly pained by them. I recall that in the era of private schools and academies, the depth of their teachers' fostering and edification was almost like the thick labor of their parents. Therefore, releasing vegetables and offering sacrifices showed the respect for the teacher's way, and private posthumous titles and heart mourning further enhanced the report of the teacher's virtue. The salary was exhausted, the fire was transmitted, and the private morality was embraced, forming its own temporary atmosphere and being able to transform the vulgar customs of the world. Scholars who maintained their character and encouraged their discipline were also countless in history. It is known that those who place importance on the influence of personality have such a great effect, and it is not said that the private schools and academies are superior to the schools.

If the consistent school education for more than ten years cannot prevent its students from being infected by the evil society, then education is equal to wasted consumption. If hundreds of millions of people from schools still cannot eliminate the vulgar customs of society, then society must return to destruction. We talk about the words and actions of students being noisy, but we do not think about paying attention to the influence of personality. How can we hope that the academic atmosphere will be rectified? We are worried about the mixed thoughts of young people, but we cannot strive for correct guidance. How can we hope that its trend will be upright? Today, the dignity of the teacher's way is completely exhausted. The change of Fengmeng shooting Yi has long been accustomed to the past. This is directly related to the teacher's own, and we must find ways to correct this evil wind. In recent years, school disturbances in various places have mostly been due to a small number of students who have abandoned themselves, and the lack of influence of teachers on weekdays seems to be a part of the reason. If education of young people requires the use of strict laws and decrees to correct their mistakes, then their way is already at the end, and it is what we educators should think deeply about. The past is a lesson, and the future is coming. Therefore, the future direction of education should be to balance the three aspects of imparting knowledge, cultivating personality, and leading thought, and to apply the work of potential influence in addition to lecturing and enlightening. The relationship between teachers and disciples is as close as that of family members, father and son. Since the affection and ambition are communicated, it is easy to receive. To set an example by one's own behavior and to influence them day and night, I hope that the general young students will not only have expertise in their studies, but also have roots in their morality. They will become useful materials for the country and society, and China's future will have hope. We educators can also plead not guilty to the world. Otherwise, if we continue to follow the old ways and do not change the old habits, it will not only be the bankruptcy of education, but also the country will not be the country. Even if we can raise hundreds of millions of dollars in funding and set up hundreds of more schools, what benefit will it have for the country and society? All these are common diseases of education in our country. I hope that everyone can understand this.

Records of Knocking on Bells in Ancient Temples (II) (II) 113

Not Removing the Courtyard Grass,齋夫 (Translator's Note: A pen name)

Twenty-Five

"Let's go outside and take a look. This temple isn't very good." Mr. Zhu said, walking towards the gate. I said, "You won't find a better place outside the temple. The village is just a bunch of thatched huts, how can they be schools? Even Zhang Huzi's house, though it has a shikumen gate, is much smaller than this old temple, definitely not suitable." Mr. Zhu said, "Let's just go take a look, it won't hurt. Zhong'er, don't be so stubborn, maybe there's a better place out there waiting for us to find it." So I led Mr. Zhu through the village. How lively! Even the young ladies and young mistresses were running to their doorways to watch, chattering like popping broad beans, saying, "That's the teacher!" The children were following behind in groups of three or five, like tails.

We walked to the blacksmith's shop. Li the blacksmith put down the red-hot iron and came out to greet us. Mr. Zhu smiled and said to me, "This shop is a great classroom, and Li the clerk is our teacher. We'll have to ask him for advice in the future." Li the clerk said politely, "Mr. Zhu, don't laugh at me. I'm just a rough man, what do I know? I'll need the teacher to guide me."

We said goodbye to Li the clerk and saw old Xu building a wall in the distance. Mr. Zhu said, "That wall-building place is also one of our classrooms, and the bricklayer clerk is also our teacher. What's that clerk's name?" "That's old Xu the bricklayer, he's the one who's against setting up a school." I told Mr. Zhu his history from beginning to end. Mr. Zhu said, "Even if he's against it, if we want to learn the principles of wall-building, we'll have to ask him."

Walking on, there was a large vegetable garden, and Zhao Xiao'er was watering it with manure. Xiao'er's vegetables are famous, big and tender and grow quickly. No one in the village can compare to him. Mr. Zhu said, "Zhao's vegetable garden is also one of our classrooms. Xiao'er is the teacher who teaches us how to grow vegetables."

Half a li from the vegetable garden was a mountain, covered with pine trees, called Wansong Ridge. There was an old pine tree on Wansong Ridge, and an old eagle was nesting on it. Mr. Zhu asked, "What is this old pine tree? And who is that old eagle?" I answered without hesitation and with complete confidence, "This old pine tree is one of our classrooms. And that old eagle is our teacher." Mr. Zhu said, "Smart Zhong'er, birds are very good architectural engineers. It is said that ancient people learned to build houses from birds. I want to ask you one more question, this place is our classroom, that place is also our classroom, so where exactly is our school?" I said, "Mr. Zhu, you've completely broken down my school. I know now what your school is in your heart. Your school has the blue sky as its roof, the earth as its floor, the twenty-eight constellations as its gates and walls, and all things are your teachers, all are your classmates, and I completely understand, all are your students. You have broken down my cage-like small school and given me a forest-like big school. How happy we are living in this vast expanse!" Mr. Zhu said, "Smart Zhong'er, you only know half of it!"

Shanghai Education After January 28th (15) 114

(Still)

(2) Fundamental Solutions: Speaking of the long-term plan for education in the war zone, we cannot help but recall the educational situation in various countries during the European War, which served as a wake-up call for us. When Germany was besieged on all sides and its economy was struggling, they proposed a large sum of money again in 1916 to implement the "Unified School" system, subsidize poor students to attend school, and in 1918, initiated the People's University to cultivate young laborers who lacked money and time. After the United States entered the war, the education sector became even more active, and teachers' salaries were greatly increased. In 1917, Congress passed the Smith-Hughes Act, allocating huge sums from the national treasury to subsidize vocational education. In 1918, Congress also passed the Smith-Bankhead Act, proposing to allocate 100 million yuan from the national treasury to subsidize civic and rural education. Other countries such as Britain, France, and Belgium, despite their busy military affairs, made every effort to maintain education. Although military expenditures were huge, educational funding increased rather than decreased. After the war, they further expanded their educational systems. This was all because they had foundations, funds, and supervisory boards or special accounting committees, with laws to protect them. Regardless of major political or military changes, educational funds were not allowed to be used for other purposes. We should imitate this approach so that the education sector can get on track and have hope for steady progress. This is a major key to addressing the root cause. Municipal primary schools should build excellent school buildings in the future. Looking back at the twelve municipal primary schools in Zhabei in the past, none of them owned their own buildings, and none of them had suitable playgrounds. This kind of deformed education was originally caused by historical evolution. Taking this opportunity, we should catch up quickly, select appropriate locations, purchase land and build buildings, and do practical work. We should also add secondary schools to benefit the citizens. The Mingqiang Middle School and Yates Girls' School, both private, have great buildings and good locations. It is heard that they are being shut down, which is deeply regrettable. It would be even better if the municipal government could purchase them and run them as middle schools. In the future, public schools will be the warp and private schools will be the weft of education in the war zone. Therefore, the status of private schools is also very important. It is best to merge two or three small-scale private schools to save money and improve efficiency. Since the goal is to cultivate citizens, there should be no distinctions. I believe everyone wants this. For large-scale private schools with vitality that has not been lost, their organizations should be strengthened, their content enriched, and their standards raised. Expanding on the old foundation will be smoother and easier to achieve. It is hoped that public and private cooperation will promote social education institutions. In view of the large number of traitors in this incident, there should be more supplementary schools, public schools, public education centers, and public libraries in the future. As for economic issues, we will discuss them later.

The above-mentioned government includes both the central and local governments because some things cannot be undertaken by the local government alone, and require the assistance of the central government. At the same time, it is especially hoped that educators and local residents will work together with the government to achieve twice the result with half the effort. It is heard that representatives from the disaster-stricken secondary schools will go to Beijing to petition, and the Shanghai Education Community's Patriotic United Association will petition the Ministry of Education for relief to schools in the Songhu war zone. Regarding this point, the reporter has two opinions: (1) Educational groups should stand together and jointly organize a "Shanghai War Zone Cultural Revival Committee," which would be organized by representatives elected from disaster-stricken cultural institutions and other educational groups. Enthusiastic individuals in education are of course also welcome to join. The most important tasks of this committee would include investigating the actual situation, formulating specific measures, raising funds, and contributing opinions to the government. (2) Instead of waiting for the public's requests, the government should proactively announce remedial measures based on the actual situation. Tongji University, Labor University, Jinan University, China Public School, Central Medical Business School, Shanghai Law School, Merchant Marine School, etc., have suffered great losses. How does the central government plan to manage them? How will ordinary private schools be subsidized to help them recover? It is hoped that good news will be announced within a few days.

This is also well known to everyone. Now, I am discussing this in general, hoping that everyone will recognize that today is a time of transition for education, and work together to correct the mistakes of the past and strive to create a new life for education. This is what I sincerely pray for.

At present, Jiangsu Province's finances are exhausted, and there are huge arrears in educational funding, which makes teachers and staff feel uneasy about their lives, and their enthusiasm for service may inevitably be dampened. This is especially true for local primary schools, where the educational life is extremely difficult. Their income is only enough to cover the cost of living, and now even this cannot be obtained. According to common sense, how can this be considered fair? It should be known that frequent natural and man-made disasters have been superimposed on each other, and the national treasury has been exhausted, which has become a widespread phenomenon throughout the country, and not only in Jiangsu Province. The social economy is bankrupt, and the lives of public officials are equally painful, and not only in the education sector. Moreover, education is incomparable to other undertakings. Today, when powerful enemies are invading and national disasters are imminent, and the Far East War is imminent, we are at the mercy of others, and the survival of the nation is at stake. If we want to save ourselves, the improvement of politics cannot be expected in a day, and the development of the economy cannot be achieved overnight. The only hope to save the country from the brink is this lifeline of education. If we do not make a spirit of sacrifice on this day, overcome all difficulties and maintain it together, then the political system will be bankrupt, the economy will be bankrupt, and education will also be bankrupt. Then we can only sit and watch the change of dynasties, the destruction of the masses, and the extinction of culture, and make the entire Chinese nation sink into the realm of beasts and insects. Therefore, we know that the key to China's survival lies in the shoulders of those engaged in education. A steadfast pine does not change its nature due to the cold winter, and only scholars can have constant virtue without constant property. Educators are the pioneers of society, so they must be able to establish their steadfast and outstanding integrity in times of hardship and distress. This is enough to show the true spirit of educators. After the European War, the German economy was plunged into the abyss of destruction, and the lives of university professors were no less difficult than ordinary laborers. They had no money to buy new shoes when they were worn out, and they sewed their own socks when they were torn. They could not afford meat even once a month, but their research and education were not abandoned because of this. Therefore, German culture, even after hundreds of battles and scars, has never declined. In a few years, it completed the great cause of revival. The ambition of our country's educators to save the country at the cost of their lives will surely not be behind others, and should not allow Germany to monopolize the glory. Today's decline in education is originally due to the fact that politics has not been put on the right track, and the chaos in politics is due to the fact that education has not been perfected. The two are mutually cause and effect, and cannot be discussed separately. Then how can we shirk our responsibilities by blaming the poor quality of politics? Since I am in charge of administration, I have also tried my best to organize local education funding and stabilize provincial funding. This should be seen by everyone. In the future, as long as I am in office, I will do my best to fulfill my responsibilities. I will also seek concrete results to alleviate the suffering of teachers and staff as much as possible, and I am unwilling to adorn myself with empty promises, and I dare not demand obligations from others unilaterally. Even my colleagues in the government recognize that education is the way to save the country and the foundation of the nation. Everything can be saved and delayed, but educational funding must be actively raised. It is only limited by economic facts that we have not been able to fully meet our expectations. This is something that cannot be helped and should be understood by everyone.

In short, the only way to save the country today is through education, and the way to revitalize education is for those in charge of administration and education to recognize their own responsibilities, unite sincerely, remember the difficulties of the country, have the determination to sacrifice their lives for their duties, not shirk responsibility, not give up halfway, and advance in different ways with loyalty and wisdom. Any difficulty must be overcome, and any hardship must be endured. Then, the revival of education in our country can be hoped for.

Although I am a member of the government, I consider myself no different from a scholar. I have never favored bureaucratic articles. What I have said here may be close to commonplace, but it is also inspired by sincerity. I hope that everyone will learn from the mistakes of education in the past and make changes, and be aware that education is the only way to save our country, and dedicate ourselves to our duties. Then, Jiangsu Province will be fortunate, and China will be fortunate. (End)

Local News

Joint Committee 124

Called Meeting Yesterday

Okazaki Formally Replied That Japanese Troops Will Withdraw Within Three to Five Days

Approved Reports from Military Attachés and Minutes of Second Meeting

Our Side Decided to File a Joint Complaint if No Response by the 15th

The Joint Committee held its third meeting at 10:00 yesterday morning to report on the monitoring of the Japanese troop withdrawal by military attachés from various countries and the handover situation on our side. It approved the minutes of the second meeting and discussed the complete withdrawal of Japanese troops. As a result, the Japanese side agreed to give a formal reply in three to five days. Otherwise, our side will formally file a joint complaint. If necessary, according to the provisions of Annex 3 of the agreement, the committee will vote on the complete withdrawal of Japanese troops. The details are as follows:

Attendees: The attendees included Chairman Craigie, Chinese Committee Member Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, Wen Yingxing, Director of the Public Security Bureau, American Committee Member Blome (representing Detrick), Military Attaché of the Embassy, British Committee Member Brennan, Consul-General, Brandt, Military Attaché (representing Sonheil), French Committee Member Meyrier, Consul-General, Pontevys, Military Attaché, Italian Committee Member Los, Secretary of the Embassy, Fatini, Military Attaché, Japanese Committee Member Okazaki (representing Murai), Naval Colonel Samejima (replacing Harada's vacancy), and the Committee Secretary, Englishman Langer, totaling thirteen people.

Approval of Minutes: The committee members arrived one after another at about 10:00. At 10:15, the meeting was declared open. Chairman Craigie rose to speak and instructed Secretary Langer to read the brief reports of the military attachés from various countries who went to Jiading, Wusong and other places to monitor the withdrawal of Japanese troops after the first meeting, and to inspect the handover by our side, as well as the minutes of the second meeting which discussed the issue of troop deployments in Songnan. After Langer finished reading, he asked both sides if any modifications were needed in the text. After the committee members considered briefly, it was declared that there were no objections and it was formally approved.

Issue of Complete Withdrawal: During the meeting, Chinese Committee Member Yu Hongjun asked the Chairman about the complete withdrawal of Japanese troops. The Chairman then instructed the Japanese Committee Member to reply. Japanese Committee Member Okazaki stood up and formally replied, "The Japanese naval authorities are currently in contact with the concession authorities to discuss the issue of troop deployments. Please wait another three to five days, and a decision can be made. A formal reply will be given at that time." The Chinese Committee Member continued to state that according to the ceasefire agreement, five weeks have passed since the Japanese troops began to withdraw, and they have not yet completely withdrawn. It is hoped that the Japanese side will sincerely handle the matter as soon as possible. Otherwise, our side will formally file a complaint with the meeting. The meeting adjourned at 11:10. After the committee members from Britain, France, Italy, and Chinese Committee Member Wen Yingxing excused themselves, Yu Hongjun met with the Japanese Committee Member and the Committee Secretary, Englishman Langer, for about 20 minutes before leaving at 11:30.

Meeting to Be Called: After the meeting, Chinese Committee Member Yu Hongjun sent a letter to the Japanese side on the same day, stating that the Japanese troop withdrawal has not yet fulfilled the provisions of the ceasefire agreement, and has been delayed. It is hoped that Representative Okazaki will urge the military authorities to withdraw the Japanese troops from Zone J and Tongwen College as soon as possible in order to maintain friendship. Otherwise, it will be submitted to the Joint Committee for discussion. According to reports, if the Chinese side submits the matter to the committee for discussion, the Chairman may, if necessary, instruct the committee to hold a vote in accordance with the provisions of Annex 3 of the agreement, and execute the decision based on a majority vote.

Taikoo Company 128

SS Shengking Encountered Danger

Ran Aground in Dense Fog Near Weihaiwei

Two Holes in the Bow, Sea Water Rushing In

Crew and Passengers Completely Rescued

Company Sent a Tugboat to Tow

The new SS Shengking, a North China liner of the British Taikoo Company, encountered fog and ran aground near Weihaiwei on its way from Shanghai to Tianjin. The ship was damaged and the passengers were rescued. The details are as follows:

From Shanghai to Tianjin: The Taikoo Company's North China route originally had three regular passenger liners, the SS Tongzhou, SS Fengtian, and SS Shuntian, traveling between Shanghai and Tianjin. Last year, due to the age of the three ships and the excessive consumption of coal, a new ship was built by the Hong Kong factory and named the SS Shengking. It set sail from Shanghai on its maiden voyage to Tianjin on March 2nd of this year and has operated nine voyages so far. At 10:00 on Saturday morning, it departed from Shanghai carrying cargo and passengers for Tianjin. On the way near Weihaiwei, dense fog occurred and the ship ran aground on a reef.

Ran Aground in Dense Fog: The SS Shengking arrived at Cape Chengshanjiao in Shandong on the evening of the 12th. Dense fog had occurred on the sea surface. There were many reefs in this area, making navigation difficult. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's SS Xin Daxin Chang and SS Xin Kang also suffered accidents and sank in this area. When the SS Shengking arrived at this place, Captain Li Dexi slowed down. At 8:30, the ship reached Qingming Island, which is only fifteen nautical miles east of Weihaiwei. The fog became heavier and the channel was blocked. It ran aground on a hidden reef on Qingming Island. The hull was stuck and could not move. Two large holes were also broken on both sides of the bow, and sea water rushed into the ship, causing the ship to be in danger.

Captain Sought Help: After the SS Shengking had the accident, Captain Li Dexi immediately sent out a distress radio signal. The first to receive the news was the British naval warship on Liugong Island. The British naval admiral immediately dispatched two destroyers, the HMS Wallflower and HMS Keppel, and a tugboat of the naval admiral, to Qingming Island to rescue the passengers on the SS Shengking.

Passengers Escaped Danger: The SS Shengking carried a total of 350 passengers from Shanghai to Tianjin, including 40 foreigners and 310 Chinese. After running aground, all the passengers on the ship gathered on the deck and released sampans and life jackets in an attempt to escape. When the two British warships arrived, the naval tugboats transported 35 Westerners and 187 Chinese to the HMS Wallflower and sent them to Weihaiwei to disembark. Some Chinese passengers were still being rescued. The 26 crew members were rescued by the HMS Keppel and also sent to Weihaiwei.

Luggage Recovered: At 7:30 yesterday morning, the Shanghai head office received a telegram about the SS Shengking accident, which only said that the ship had run aground and the passengers were safe. After the company telegraphed to inquire about the cause, it received a reply in the afternoon stating that all passengers had been rescued to Weihaiwei, and each person's luggage had also been transferred to Weihaiwei. It is heard that all the mail and other items have also been unloaded, and there should be no losses.

Protection and Transportation of Passengers: The company urgently telegraphed the SS Fengtian, which was en route in North China, yesterday to rush to Weihaiwei to load the rescued passengers and send them to Tianjin. As the SS Shengking had a lot of cargo loaded in Shanghai, mainly piece goods and tea, and the ship ran aground and was not immediately out of danger, it was agreed with the British Navy to send a destroyer to berth there for protection.

Towing the Hull: There are two holes in the bow of the SS Shengking, and the sea water has flooded the hold. Therefore, the cargo in the bow hold has been damaged by water and the losses are quite heavy. However, the hull is stranded on the reef and can only be towed out when the tide rises. The company was extremely busy yesterday handling the rescue work and sent the SS Ningbo to sail from Shanghai to the accident site today to handle towing and other work.

Overview of the Vessel: The SS Shengking was newly built last year and came to Shanghai from the dock in February of this year. It has only been operating for nine voyages. The ship is well constructed, with a length of 300 feet, a width of 46 feet, and a load capacity of 3,000 tons. The construction cost of the ship and the layout of each cabin is worth 1 million yuan, making it the best and fastest ship currently sailing in North China.

SS Shuntian Startled: This time, the SS Shuntian, which was coming from Tianjin to Shanghai, also suffered a major danger when passing through the waters of Cape Chengshanjiao. According to the crew of the ship, the SS Shuntian was in the middle of the night when it arrived at Cape Chengshanjiao, and there was also dense fog on the sea. A Japanese ship came head-on without sounding its whistle. When it was discovered, it was only more than ten yards away. The two ships were traveling on the same straight line. The captain of the SS Shuntian was startled and quickly reversed the engine. Fortunately, the action was quick and he was able to avoid it. If he had been a minute late, the two ships would have collided and sunk. Afterwards, a lot of sea water was pumped out of the ship. Even thinking about it now is frightening.

Reuters Weihaiwei 13th: The naval tugboat SS Saint Breock towed a cargo ship with coolie workers at 2 pm today to assist the SS Shengking in unloading cargo. The SS Huizhou is now berthed next to the SS Shengking, awaiting the arrival of the SS Fengtian from Tanggu. The cargo ship towed by the SS Saint Breock will unload cargo from the SS Shengking and transport it to the SS Fengtian, while the SS Huizhou will carry the passengers of the SS Shengking to Tanggu. The weather is good at the moment, but the fog has not yet cleared.

Both China Merchants Bureau and Butterfield & Swire Deny Taking Out Loans 129

The Kwok Wen News Agency reports: Yesterday, various newspapers in this city carried reports about the China Merchants Bureau borrowing 30 million yuan from the American firm Butterfield & Swire to reorganize its affairs. Yesterday, reporters inquired about this matter from various parties, and it was found that the facts were quite different from what was reported. Both the China Merchants Bureau and Butterfield & Swire have denied the loan. The following is a record of the statements from both parties and the details of the matter:

Li Guojie's Statement: After the news was published in various newspapers yesterday, reporters rushed to Li Guojie, the general manager of the China Merchants Bureau, to inquire. Mr. Li denied the report, saying that since he took office, the reorganization plan of the bureau has been in its initial stages. Although the China Merchants Bureau needs a large sum of 30 million yuan, it has not been carried out due to various reasons since he took office. The reports in the newspapers are either rumors or inaccurate.

Butterfield & Swire's Denial: The reporter went to Butterfield & Swire at 3 Guangdong Road and requested to see the company's manager to inquire about the matter. The reply was that in this time of global commercial depression, the existing business is already overwhelming, and the company denies lending 30 million yuan to the China Merchants Bureau and declares that it is a misrepresentation.

Ministry of Communications Once Had Such a Proposal: The idea of the China Merchants Bureau taking out a loan has been around since the time of Zhao Tieqiao. After Zhao was murdered, the matter was shelved. When Li Zhonggong was appointed as commissioner, he suggested taking out a loan to the Ministry of Communications, but it was not successful because the conditions were not met. When Guo Waifeng succeeded Li as commissioner, someone also suggested it to Mr. Guo, but Mr. Guo did not dare to act rashly because he thought it was a big matter. When Chen Fumu continued as supervisor, the Ministry of Communications, in view of the China Merchants Bureau's heavy debt burden and inability to develop its business, recently had the idea of taking out a loan. It is rumored that although there are major industrialists willing to invest, it has not yet become a reality because the conditions are not right.

Adding Shipping Routes Also Inaccurate: The Kwok Wen News Agency reports that it has been widely rumored recently that the China Merchants Bureau Steamship Company plans to borrow 30 million yuan from the American firm Butterfield & Swire Steamship Company to repay debts and expand its shipping fleet. A reporter from the Kwok Wen News Agency specially visited Mr. Li Guojie, the general manager of the bureau, yesterday to ask if this was true. Mr. Li said that he did not know where this news came from and that he had no knowledge of it. He is now investigating the matter after seeing it in the newspaper and hopes that the public will not believe it. It is also reported that the bureau has purchased two Norwegian merchant ships and plans to officially start operating them at the beginning of next month, adding shipping routes to Southeast Asia. This is also inaccurate because the two ships, "Hai Rui" and "Hai Xiang," were purchased last year as cargo ships and cannot carry passengers. They have been transporting goods for a long time (with no fixed routes). All ships will have new schedules when the situation becomes peaceful and the transportation of troops is over, and it is not just for the above two ships.

Wang Pingnan Led the Volunteer Army Back to Shanghai Yesterday 134

A Portion Stayed in Wuxi for Training to Go to the Border to Fight the Enemy

Wang Pingnan, a member of the Volunteer Army Committee of the Shanghai Citizens' Federation and the second captain of the Volunteer Army Student Regiment accompanying the 19th Route Army, led the army back to Shanghai yesterday. According to Mr. Wang, the second team has 234 volunteers, including 53 who volunteered to go to the Northeast to help eliminate the Japanese invaders. They are currently staying in Wuxi, led by Captain Li Xiangheng, to continue training under Brigade Commander Weng. The first team of university students and the second team of the Nanjing Iron Blood Corps also have 50 to 60 people staying in Wuxi. As soon as the transportation question is solved, they will set off north. After the volunteer army of this team (the second team) returned to Shanghai, those from nearby and neighboring provinces left on their own. There are still 53 people from Sichuan and Guangdong, and 97 people from the first and third teams, who are unable to return to their hometowns because of the long distance, road obstruction, and lack of travel funds. Although they remain in Shanghai, their situation is very difficult. After graduating on June 10, the first and third teams were given four yuan each by Brigade Commander Weng, and the second team was given ten yuan each by the Citizens' Federation, but this was not enough for the long journey. Chen Qianfu is now running around to appeal to the Sichuan and Guangdong associations and other patriotic organizations to raise travel funds so that the patriotic volunteers will not suffer the hardships of being stranded in a foreign land because of their dedication to fighting against Japan.

Fourteen students from Southeast University took the night train from Shanghai to Beijing last night and then went to the Northeast to join the battlefield and take on medical rescue work.

Telegrams from the Jianghuai and Gaoyou Associations

The Jiangbei area has always been plagued by bandits, but fortunately, Pacification Commissioner Zhang has been effective in suppressing them, which has allowed them to be slightly restrained. However, due to years of famine and hardship, the people are suffering, and bandits are taking the opportunity to launch attacks. Gaoyou was hit by floods last year, and thanks to Pacification Commissioner Zhang's active rescue efforts, countless dying people were saved. We represent the people of Gaoyou and beg you to reconsider. The Gaoyou Fellow Association."

Requests the National Government to Exempt Taxes in the Disaster Area

The Industrial and Commercial Reconstruction Committee in the disaster area of this city, in view of the fact that the Zhabei, Jiangwan, and Wusong areas suffered a great disaster after the Shanghai Incident, in order to maintain the recovery of industry and commerce in the disaster area, specially submitted a document to the National Government yesterday, requesting that all taxes in the disaster area be exempted to alleviate the people's suffering. The original document stated: "We are submitting this request to exempt taxes in the disaster area to alleviate industry and commerce. Unfortunately, our country is plagued by floods and droughts, and bandits are everywhere. All industries are suffering, and internal wars are frequent. The sound of gunfire is everywhere, and the people are not living. The government is already exhausting all its resources, and taxes and miscellaneous fees are increasing endlessly. The state is doing its utmost to drain the pond to get all the fish, and the people are suffering more and more. In recent years, industry and commerce have been declining, and the state of hardship is indescribable. Since the January 28th Incident, the Zhabei, Jiangwan, and Wusong areas have been reduced to battlefields, with scars everywhere and scorched earth. It is unknown when they will recover. The Shanghai authorities, in order to relieve the suffering, have established the Shanghai War Zone Relief Committee and other organizations, which have been established for two weeks. However, we have only seen the empty words of proclamations and have not received any practical relief. We lament the suffering of our industry and commerce. The current hardships are as such, and the future disasters are still not over. We dare to appeal to Your Excellency to exempt all national taxes first to alleviate the suffering and leave a glimmer of hope for industry and commerce. It is also to protect the foundation of China and preserve the livelihood of the people. We respectfully request that you examine and approve our request and order its implementation to help industry and commerce. This will be fortunate for the public. We respectfully submit to the National Government."

Household Survey of Wusong Yinhing 141

Two Thousand Three Hundred and Ninety-Six Households

More Than Eleven Thousand Seven Hundred People

Since the Japanese invasion of Shanghai, the Municipal Public Security Bureau has been conducting a census of all households in the disaster area. The bureau's statistics are as follows: (1) Wusong Township: 580 households, 8 vacant households, 1,266 males, 1,472 females; (2) Yinhing Town: 191 households, 13 vacant households, 464 males, 403 females; (3) Yinhing Township: 1,467 households, 137 vacant households, 3,893 males, 4,231 females. Total: 2,238 households, 158 vacant households, 5,623 males, 6,106 females. Total: 2,396 households, 11,729 males and females.

Municipal Government Convened a Meeting with Workers of the Sanyou Factory 142

The Capitalist Side Agreed to Pay Retirement Funds

Workers Want to Resume Work

The Shanghai Municipal Government, in view of the prolonged dispute over the closure of the Sanyou Factory, which has lasted for four months without a resolution, specially sent staff member Yuan Shenglu to convene a meeting with representatives of the Sanyou Union yesterday afternoon. Wang Bing, a representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, Xia Zhongzhao and Gong Liangshi, representatives of the Sanyou Union, were present. The representative of the Municipal Government stated that the capitalist side of Sanyou did not intend to resume work and did not formally announce the dismissal, but agreed to pay one month's salary as retirement funds, and promised to give priority to hiring them when the factory reopens. After listening to the statement, the union representatives said that the capitalist's move was unexpected and was actually a deliberate oppression of the workers. Since there were so many retirement funds to dismiss the workers, why did they claim that they did not have enough funds to resume business? Their intentions were self-evident, so they declared their rejection and asked the authorities to order the capitalist side to maintain the workers' livelihood and resume work as soon as possible to prevent the dispute from escalating.

Telephone Workers in the Concession to Protest to the Company Today 143

Implement Reorganization of the Strike Committee

General Meeting Was Prevented by the Police Last Night

Discipline Promulgated, a Foreman Was Beaten

The New Voice News Agency reports that the telephone workers in the concession have been on strike for seven days. After the company issued a notice to the workers, the situation has become more serious. The workers held an emergency meeting and decided to protest to the company today. The strike committee has issued a notice to the workers to strictly abide by discipline. The details are as follows:

Temporary General Meeting: The strike committee held a temporary emergency meeting at the Tongshang Hotel on Avenyue Road at 10:00 p.m. the day before yesterday and decided: (1) Some members of the strike committee will be dismissed immediately due to their poor performance and will be reorganized. New members will be elected to supplement the committee, and the total number will remain at 21; (2) Improve the organization of the strike committee; (3) Adopt effective measures to negotiate with the company again; (4) All workers will gather at the New Central Bank on Fujian Road on the morning of the 13th to urge the company to reply; (5) Protest against the company's notice to the workers.

Urging Reply: At 10:00 a.m. yesterday, the striking workers were ordered to gather at the New Central Bank on Fujian Road to urge the company to officially reply to the conditions. However, because of the small number of participants and the absence of responsible personnel from the company, the gathering was stopped and a meeting was held at the Zaichun Pavilion on Zhejiang Road. It was decided: (1) to expand the strike organization; (2) to hold a general meeting of all workers on Heard Road at 2:00 p.m. to solicit the opinions of the workers and then decide on the course of action.

Strictly Abide by Discipline: After the company issued a notice to the workers, the strike committee specially issued a notice to all workers yesterday morning, stating: "For the notice, the attitude of the capitalist side towards the conditions we have put forward is extremely tough and has obviously broken down. It is necessary to continue the strike. All workers are not allowed to go to work and must abide by discipline. Anyone who violates this privately will be punished by this court in accordance with the law and will not be forgiven." To all workers, the strike committee court secretariat. (The strike discipline is as follows: (1) No one is allowed to go to work privately without the order of the strike committee; (2) No one except the representatives sent by the strike committee may negotiate with the capitalist side; (3) Obey the command and orders of the strike committee. Anyone who violates the above discipline will be treated as a traitor.

Protest Today: Subsequently, because the former police station of Jinan University prohibited the assembly, the meeting could not be held. Therefore, the strike committee was reorganized and decided: At 10:00 a.m. today, each department of the nine branches, including the General Company on Jiangxi Road, the Fujian Road, Haining Road, Yidingpan Road, Mintiniyin Road, and Yangshupu branches, will send one representative, together with three representatives from the presidium of the strike committee, to the company to protest to the manager and urge him to reply to the conditions.

Emergency Notice: The strike committee issued a notice to all workers yesterday: (1) Tomorrow (the 14th), each branch and department must convene a mass meeting, and the presidium can send a person in charge to attend and report. Please inform Zhu Jun of the meeting time and location determined by the responsible representatives of each branch and department by 9:00 a.m. tomorrow (the 14th); (2) The presidium has decided to submit a letter of protest to the capitalist side at 10:00 a.m. tomorrow (the 14th) and urge it to reply to the conditions. We hope that each branch and department will quickly send one representative to set off together with the representatives designated by the presidium. All representatives must gather here by 9:00 a.m. tomorrow; (3) The disciplinary committee must perform its duties in accordance with the order of the temporary general meeting from today onwards.

Original Text of the Protest: The Telephone Workers' Strike Committee protested the telephone company's notice to the workers as follows: (1) The company said, "The strike was not notified to the company in advance" and "The company is willing to discuss any issues raised in accordance with the company's procedures." These are lies to deceive the workers and cover up the truth. Last year, the workers submitted 18 requests to the company and asked them to discuss and reply, but the company ignored them. This year, the foreman asked the workers to sign their names, requesting the company to increase wages, but there was no reply. Recently, they asked to restore the jobs of the dismissed workers, but the company ignored them. The company completely does not take Chinese workers into account and is unwilling to discuss the workers' problems. Therefore, the workers have learned a lesson and have no way out but to resort to the means of strike to deal with the company and solve the workers' own problems. Therefore, the responsibility for the strike and the responsibility for sacrificing public convenience should be entirely borne by the company, and the workers cannot bear any responsibility; (2) "The internal reorganization plan of the company" is to cancel Sunday pay, Sunday rest, and wages are paid as usual. Working on Sundays, wages are doubled. It used to be like this, what "reorganization plan" is going to cancel the regulations for working on Sundays and doubling wages. The company wants the workers to work on Sundays without doubling their wages. This is just forced labor. The so-called "reorganization plan" is just a plan to attack the workers twice as much; (3) "The company's workers' salaries in April will not increase due to business relations." The company "due to business relations" (note that it is not that the company lost money, but that the business is going to make a lot of money), can increase the price of telephones, reduce the workers' wages, and dismiss the workers, all of which are "legitimate." Workers ask for a little wage increase because prices have risen and they can't fill their stomachs, which is an "unreasonable" request. Workers are dismissed and have no food to eat, and they ask for a little retirement money, which is also an "unreasonable" request. This is just sophistry. Such "legitimacy" and "truth" are just another name for oppressing the workers; (4) "The company did not deduct pension money and savings money." But when the company dismisses workers, it always uses various excuses. In fact, most of it is deducted. We firmly oppose deducting workers' savings in any way; (5) "The company is undergoing a reorganization plan," "It must dismiss a large number of workers." We firmly oppose the company's "reorganization plan" to oppress and sacrifice workers. We demand the protection of workers' lives and interests. We are completely legitimate; (6) "The strike is instigated by a small number of bad elements, and the workers are being fooled." This is slander and insult to the workers, and it is a poisonous trick to split the workers. Old pigs also resist when they are oppressed. Our workers are not even as good as old pigs. When we are oppressed to the point where we cannot breathe, we do not know to rise up and resist. The workers are all wooden heads who only know how to be fooled. When they are hungry, they don't even know to eat. The imperialist capitalists look down on the Chinese people even more than pigs. Three thousand workers strike unanimously and insist on striking. This is an iron fact. The workers will not fall for the capitalists' tricks. They are united to fight for their demands and resolutely support their leaders. They will fight the capitalists to the end so that the imperialists dare not underestimate the Chinese people. We must fight for our own interests and also fight for the dignity of the Chinese nation. The company is still unwilling to discuss the three conditions with the workers today and refuses to meet with the workers' representatives. It has no sincerity in resolving the strike. The company should bear the responsibility for the extension of the strike and the impact on the public's convenience. We hope that all sectors of society will warn the capitalists to reply to the workers' conditions and resolve the strike as soon as possible, and give the workers sympathy and assistance.

Foreman Was Beaten: When the telephone workers unanimously insisted on striking, a certain foreman was recruited by the capitalist side to gather workers and go to work privately. The workers were very angry. Dozens of workers surrounded and beat him yesterday evening, causing him serious injuries. It is reported that the company has sent the foreman to the hospital and dare not recruit workers to start work again.

Notice to Workers: The Shanghai Telephone Company Workers' Strike Committee's notice to workers: "All workers, we have been on strike for six days to oppose the company's dismissal, demand increased wages, and retirement funds. The capitalist not only did not reply to our conditions, but also dismissed twelve of our workers. The capitalist said, 'The strike was not notified to the company in advance,' and 'The company manager is happy to discuss the workers' problems with the workers.' These are lies. In the past, we signed and submitted to the company, but the company completely ignored us and did not discuss it. Therefore, we had to use strike to oppose the capitalist. The capitalist does not treat us workers as human beings. He is preparing to starve us workers to death. He does not talk to our representatives. Can we still tolerate such oppression and insult from the capitalist? We must use our blood to fight the capitalist to the death. The strike committee calls on the workers to insist on striking to the end. We swear not to go to work if the capitalist does not agree to our conditions. The capitalist has sent traitors and lackeys everywhere to spread rumors and notify the workers to go to work. Workers, do not listen to the capitalist's rumors. Beat the traitors and lackeys. Lackeys have also been found in the presidium of the strike committee. At the presidium meeting yesterday, Weng Zhenhua, Chen Zherong, and Pan Mou proposed three resolutions: (1) As long as the capitalist agrees to 'recognize the trade union' and Sunday work, they can go to work. The articles on wage increases, job security, and retirement funds are no longer needed; (2) Go to the Kuomintang to petition for mediation; (3) Dismiss committee member Ye Gongxing. Workers, we must insist on striking until we win the conditions before we go to work, but the members of the presidium, Chen et al., want to go to work and sacrifice the workers' conditions. We want the representatives of the strike committee to directly negotiate with the capitalists for a solution because the result of asking someone to mediate the postal and newspaper strikes was the failure of the strike, with no conditions and many workers arrested. We do not want the strike to be the same as the postal and newspaper strikes, so we oppose mediation, but they insist on asking the Kuomintang to mediate. Ye Gongxing, as a representative, works hard for the workers. Only the police and capitalists oppose Ye Gongxing, arrest him, but Weng Chen et al. want to dismiss Ye Gongxing. Workers, is this not the action of traitors and lackeys? Can such a presidium lead us to victory in the strike? Absolutely not. Therefore, the representative assembly held an emergency meeting yesterday afternoon, unanimously denied the above resolutions passed by the presidium, reorganized the presidium, dismissed all the positions of Weng Zhenhua, Chen Zherong, Pan Mou, etc., and re-elected Ye Gongxing and other eleven people to form the presidium, leading the workers to fight to the end and win the conditions. The new presidium is willing to use their lives and leadership to fight for the victory of the strike. Everyone must obey the orders of the strike committee and support the strike committee to fight together. We are not just acting on emotion. Because the old presidium wants to sell out the workers, we must fight for the victory of the strike, and we must drive them out. Driving them out will not reduce our strength, but will make our unity more consolidated and our leadership stronger. Workers, unite, overthrow the lackeys, insist on striking, and victory is ours. Shanghai Telephone Company Strike Committee, June 13."

Our province is unfortunate to have suffered from the scourge of bandits for a long time, in deep water and scorching fire. However, tracing its origin, it is due to the corruption of politics and the provincial government authorities using the buying off of bandits to build their personal power, leading to the intensification of the bandit atmosphere and the lack of peaceful days for the people. Anti-Drug Association Requests 146

Executive Yuan to Announce Anti-Opium Stance

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, based on recent investigations and reports in various newspapers, has learned that the central authorities, facing financial exhaustion and helplessness, are vigorously promoting the public sale of opium and are determined to implement it. Yesterday, the association sent a telegram to Wang Jingwei, the president of the Executive Yuan, inquiring about the truth of the matter and requesting a clear announcement of the anti-opium stance. At the same time, the association sent a telegram to national public organizations and party headquarters at all levels, calling on them to jointly advocate against opium. The telegram is recorded as follows: "Most urgent, To Wang Jingwei, President of the Executive Yuan of the National Government, Since the past two months, the central government has been planning the public sale of opium, and rumors have been rampant, causing public discontent. Our association has repeatedly inquired of your esteemed Yuan through letters and telegrams to ascertain the truth. Furthermore, believing that the current National Government, which takes the people's will as its center and has been baptized by the Three Principles of the People, would never go so far as to implement the public sale of opium, we dared not believe the rumors from near and far. Unexpectedly, unfortunate facts have suddenly come to light. According to yesterday's Shanghai Japanese-language Mainichi Shimbun, the central government, facing financial exhaustion and helplessness, is determined to implement the public sale of opium. Yesterday evening, the Shanghai Da Wan Bao and this morning's Shen Bao also published similar news. Upon reading these reports, we were shocked and ashamed. According to Premier Sun Yat-sen's anti-drug instructions, "The war against opium must never be compromised or abandoned. If the responsible government agency, for its own convenience and immediate interests, lowers the flag and ceases the war against opium, no matter how brief, it is an act of treason." This shows that opium is an item that Premier Sun Yat-sen detested and resolutely rejected, and it is also regarded as a deadly enemy by the people. However, the central financial authorities have been thinking about it day and night, coveting it for a long time, and using various tricks to seek its implementation. Our association has sent many letters and telegrams, but your esteemed Yuan has not replied, and the situation can be imagined. Recently, Liu Ruiheng, chairman of the Anti-Opium Committee, has opposed the immediate prohibition and advocated a gradual prohibition, and Finance Minister Song Ziwen has resolutely resigned. Rumors have also spread that these are closely related to the public sale of opium. Now, reading the above-mentioned news reports, it seems to have been confirmed. The people of the whole country feel uneasy and at a loss because they have not received a clear reply from your esteemed Yuan. Our association, therefore, represents the public opinion and sends another telegram to inquire and express our views. If the central government is determined to proceed without considering the alternatives, the people will swear to oppose it to the death and will never surrender. Our association is determined to fight against drugs and will fight to the end. We earnestly request your esteemed Yuan to provide a concrete reply as soon as possible to dispel public opinion. We await your instructions with utmost urgency. The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, respectfully, Yuan Yin."

China's Participation in the Chicago World's Fair 147

Preparatory Committee to be Established Tomorrow

The Chicago World's Fair in the United States is scheduled to open next year (1932). The Ministry of Industry, on the orders of the National Government, will participate in the fair. The progress of the preparations for the fair is as follows:

First Preparatory Committee Meeting Tomorrow Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo has been appointed to preside over all the preparations. The office will be located in the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry on the fourth floor of the Jianghai Customs Building on Hankou Road. Tomorrow (the 15th) at 2:00 p.m., the Preparatory Committee for China's Participation in the Chicago World's Fair will hold its first meeting at the Bank Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road to discuss all matters.

Sixty Invitations Sent to Preparatory Committee Members The Ministry of Industry, recognizing the great international importance of the fair, which is unlike ordinary exhibitions, has sent letters to leaders of industry and commerce in China, inviting them to serve as preparatory committee members. A total of sixty people, including Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Gongquan, and Chen Guangfu, are among those invited.

Minister Chen Scheduled to Host Reception Tomorrow Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo is scheduled to host a reception for the preparatory committee members at the Bank Club at No. 4 Hong Kong Road tomorrow (the 15th) at 12:00 noon. Invitations have already been distributed.

Organizational Structure of the Preparatory Committee The regulations for the committee were promulgated by the National Government on May 21st of this year. The committee will have four departments: general affairs, exhibition, publicity, and administration. The Minister of Industry, Chen Gongbo, will serve as the chairman of the committee. There will be seven to nine standing committee members and sixty preparatory committee members. Minister Chen has already sent invitations to leaders from all sectors to serve as members.
