Harbor Quarantine Station 150

Third Cholera Weekly Report

Dr. Wu Liande of the Harbor Quarantine Station released the third cholera weekly report yesterday (the 13th), stating: (1) The cholera situation in Shanghai in the past week (up to June 11) was similar to the previous week. After bacteriological examination, there were a total of 90 patients (including 90 deaths). A brief summary is as follows: A. Shanghai Number of patients Number of deaths

Chinese area 52 7

Public Concession 29 1

French Concession 9 1

Total 90 9

Total in the previous week 190 23 Total number of cases this year 280 22

B. Shanghai Epidemic Hospital 64 2

Emergency Epidemic Hospital 12 4

Public Shanghai Hospital 6 2

IC Isolation Hospital 8 2

Total 90 9

(2) Cholera has also been discovered in other Chinese ports. A) An American expatriate in Qufu, who came from Shanghai, arrived on June 6, fell ill the next day, and died that evening. B) Cholera was first discovered in Nanjing on May 18. As of June 4, there were a total of 20 patients (including 12 deaths). (3) Following the Dutch East Indies and Singapore, Hong Kong also announced on June 8 that Shanghai was an infected port, and Japan had a similar announcement on June 9. (4) The Shanghai Port Quarantine Administration notified the various port authorities on June 9 that they should simultaneously prevent the invasion of cholera from Shanghai. These ports include Xiamen, Shantou, Guangzhou, Qingdao, Qufu, Qinhuangdao, Tanggu, Tianjin, Andong, and Yingkou. (5) The Chinese Red Cross Society has established the First Cholera Alert Hospital on Xinmin Road in Zhabei, which can accommodate 300 people, and the Second Cholera Hospital on Mei Baike Road, which can accommodate 150 people. In addition, there is the Hongkou Epidemic Hospital, located on Tangshan Road in Hongkou (between Gongping Road and Dengtuo Road), which can accommodate 500 patients. (6) Two notable cases of cholera patients are briefly described below. A. Mrs. Xu, female, 40 years old, four months pregnant, suffered from severe vomiting and diarrhea. On June 9, she sought treatment at the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital on Xizang Road. After being admitted to the hospital, she was given saline injections, which greatly reduced her pain. The next day, she had a miscarriage. According to the patient, she is still recovering in the hospital. After bacteriological examination, it was confirmed that she had genuine cholera. (7) The Central Committee for the Prevention of Cholera convenes weekly meetings of the health authorities of the Chinese and Concession areas at the Harbor Quarantine Station to discuss publicity work and investigate the source of the disease. These meetings are held in rotation. As a result of last month's meeting, cholera films can be shown in various theaters. Preventive vaccination work is still being carried out as usual. (8) The issue of drinking water for the poor is an urgent matter at the moment and is being addressed to improve the situation. There are a total of four tap water plants in Shanghai:

A. Shanghai City Nanshi Water Plant, capable of serving 500,000 people.

Wusong Water Plant, capable of serving 1.5 million people.

The cost is 50 cents per 1,000 gallons.

B. Public Concession Yangshupu Water Plant, capable of serving 1.5 million people.

The cost is 62.5 cents per 1,000 gallons.

C. French Concession Nanshi Water Plant, capable of serving 600,000 people.

The cost is 59 cents per 1,000 gallons. (9) The most disadvantaged can only use unclean water from nearby rivers, wells, and ponds. Even those who do not use it for drinking often use it to wash clothes, utensils, and food. Therefore, the occurrence of cholera is an important reason. (10) The French Concession has public tap water pipes that are free of charge. The Public Concession does not have this kind of facility. Tap water pipes should be installed in places with clean drinking water, and the public should be supplied with it. The public should also be persuaded to use it. Recent observations show that cholera is only widespread in Shanghai this year, and other ports may also be spared.

The Shanghai County Farmers' Education Hall is holding an exhibition to promote native cloth. For several days, it has been touring the districts of Zhuanqiao, Minhang, and Maqiao in turn. Local News Two

After Three Deaths from Shell Explosion 153

Old Mother Dies Upon Hearing News

Jiang Luoshi Escapes Death

How Will Huang Qian Face His Old Mother in the Afterlife?

Cantonese Chen Guojun, Huang Qian, and their fellow villager Mr. Ye jointly rented a tailor shop at No. 531 and a half Hongan Lane, Bazilu, and lived in the front wing room on the ground floor. The rear wing room was rented to Cantonese young women Liang Shengyu and Jiang Luoshi. At 2:00 p.m. the day before yesterday, Chen, Huang, and Ye, having nothing to do, went to Zhabei to visit the war ruins. On the way back, they picked up a shell with a diameter of about two and a half inches and brought it home. After dinner, Chen took out the shell and fondled it. The men and women living together gathered around to watch. Only Jiang Luoshi had deeper insight and believed that such dangerous items should not be treated as toys to avoid causing disaster. She repeatedly asked Chen to find a way to discard it. However, Chen did not listen to good advice, and the others also ridiculed her for being overly concerned. Therefore, although the speaker spoke earnestly, the listeners despised her. Seeing that honest advice was unwelcome, Jiang Luoshi went to bed. As soon as she got into bed, she suddenly heard a loud bang, and disaster struck. After Jiang Luoshi went out, Chen and the others continued to fondle and stroke the shell even more. Chen accidentally dropped the shell on the ground, and it exploded instantly. When Jiang Luoshi came out again, she saw that the three men and one woman who had been watching were all injured and lying on the ground, covered in blood and flesh. The scene was unbearable. Chen Guojun and Huang Qian were the most seriously injured and were killed on the spot. Mr. Ye and Liang Shengyu were still alive. Jiang Luoshi reported to the Hongkou police station and the relatives of the dead and injured. Soon, Chinese and foreign detectives and Chen's younger brother Guochang and Huang's cousin Qicong arrived. After the detectives inquired about the cause of the accident, they sent Mr. Ye to Tongren Hospital and Liang Shengyu to Guangren Hospital for treatment. The bodies of Chen and Huang were taken to the Filen Road morgue. However, Liang died before receiving treatment after arriving at the hospital. The hospital notified the police station, which sent detectives to the morgue. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court sent prosecutor Li Ying to the morgue to examine the bodies and question them. The court ordered Chen's body to be handed over to his younger brother Chen Guochang, Huang's body to his cousin Huang Qicong, and Liang's body to her friend Chen Jiangshi, who signed guarantees to take them away for burial. However, Huang Qian's mother, who lived on Kangnao Road, was old. That night, she suddenly heard the shocking news and mourned the untimely death of her son. She wanted to rush to the scene of the accident, but she was too old to do so. Therefore, her crying became even more sorrowful. Unexpectedly, she died of grief. It was truly tragic. Now, the police station believes that such tragedies have occurred frequently after the war. It is due to ignorant and foolish people causing their own disasters. It is hoped that the general public will learn from the past and not lightly pick up explosive objects. They should report to the nearest police station to have them destroyed to avoid future troubles.

Ye Xianglian Has No Involvement

Kidnappers' Furniture Confiscated

After Yan Yutang of Dalong Iron Factory, Meilun Textile Factory, and Guangyu Business Company was kidnapped, Chief Inspector Lu Liankui and Inspector Liu Shaokui of the General Patrol and Inspection Office, together with all the detectives, rescued Yan at No. 72 Pushi Road and arrested six kidnappers, Wang Jian, Kong Ali, Chen Huiqing, Chen Xiaosi, Yang Jingzhai, and Ye Xianglian, confiscated three box cannons, one poison gas pistol, and more than 140 bullets, and sent them to the First Special Court for interrogation. Hartung Couple

Legally Married

Judgment of the English Registrar

The estate case of the deceased wealthy businessman Hartung was heard several times by the English Registrar last week. The plaintiff argued that Hartung was an Iraqi and should be dealt with according to Iraqi law. They also claimed that Jewish law does not recognize the marriage between a Jew and a non-Jew. The defendant's lawyer strongly refuted the plaintiff's claim on the issue of Hartung's wife's identity and argued that the deceased Hartung was British and should be dealt with according to English law. After the English Registrar continued the hearing yesterday morning, the Registrar, Grace, ruled on the marriage issue, stating that the Hartung couple were legally married. The plaintiff had failed to provide evidence to prove that the marriage was illegal according to English law. The defendant's lawyer then continued to argue the issue of the deceased Hartung's British nationality, presenting six points, stating that according to the Privy Council's order, Hartung should be British: 1. He was British according to the Privy Council's order. 2. He died in China, so his will and property should naturally be under the jurisdiction of the English Registrar. 3. Such cases should be under the jurisdiction of the court of the deceased's residence and handled in accordance with the laws stipulated in the treaty. The issue of nationality is not actually very important. 4. The deceased was under British protection, and the British King taxed his property, so he was naturally British in fact. 5. The deceased served as a director of the Shanghai Municipal Council on behalf of the British community during his lifetime. 6. When the Chinese government awarded him medals, it recognized him as British.

A Manufacturing Facility Uncovered on Yaozhu Road

Zhao Youming and Yongxiang, from Sichuan, recently jointly rented a Western-style house at No. 112 Yaozhu Road in the French Concession, setting up a private morphine manufacturing facility. They secretly manufactured and sold it, making a considerable profit. Unexpectedly, the matter was discovered by Lu Jinbao and Cao Fuchang, detectives from the Beidang Road French Concession Police Department. They reported to the police chief, who, along with Western detective Lü Aicai (transliteration), rushed to search the premises at 2:00 AM on the 12th. It was already late at night, and the people in the house were asleep. The detectives knocked on the door and entered. On the third floor, they seized manufacturing machinery, motors, and a large number of manufacturing equipment, such as porcelain sand filter tanks, funnels, large and small glass tanks and bottles, medicinal materials, and seventeen packages of dry and wet powder, weighing 394 and 3/4 catties (being finished and unfinished morphine raw materials), worth over 100,000 gold. Hou Yunshan, Jin Yushan, the cook Liu Mingzhang, and coolies Hou Lihe and Tu Hongfa, five people in charge of the house, were arrested on the spot. However, Zhao and Ou were not at the premises, but lived in another residence. Hou and the other five were taken to the police station along with the machinery, etc., and temporarily detained. At noon that day, Zhao and Ou were also arrested. Yesterday, they were escorted to the Second Special District Local Court for investigation. At 3:00 PM, Judge Wu Fanglian (originally Judge Xiong Huiping's court session, but Wu substituted due to Xiong's leave) and registrar Fei Zongkan came to the First Criminal Court for interrogation. First, Fei Xizhen, a lawyer from the police station, stated the case, saying, "The police station discovered a manufacturing site for opium substitutes on the third floor of No. 121 Yaozhu Road at 2:00 AM on the 12th, arresting the third to seventh defendants at the time, and the first and second defendants were arrested later. Now, they are being prosecuted under Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law. However, the police station has not yet completed the procedures due to the time of investigation, so it requests that the incriminating evidence be stored in the warehouse first and that a hearing be granted for further investigation at a later date." After Judge Wu briefly questioned the defendants, he approved a postponement of the hearing to the 16th. The defendants were detained, and the seized items were stored in the warehouse.

Zhao Xilin Shot by Enemies 157

Seriously Injured, Life in Danger

Zhao Xilin, 33 years old, from Changzhou, lives at No. 24 Shoude Lane, Yangshupu Road. He used to be a detective in his hometown of Wujin County, and his work was highly valued by his superiors. Recently, he has also been working in Shanghai as an inspector at the Shenxin No. 9 Cotton Mill and as a security guard at the China First Sock Factory. He also runs the Leyi Lou beach volleyball court at No. 40 Songpan Road. Because of this, Zhao sometimes comes to Shanghai to handle public and private affairs. In July of last year, Zhao arrested a large number of communists in Wujin County and punished them according to the law, which caused them to bear a grudge and plan to harm him. Soon after, Zhao became aware of this and secretly came to Shanghai to avoid their attacks. However, the bandits followed him and were forced to attack him once, hitting him with two shots. Fortunately, they were not fatal. After medical treatment at Tongren Hospital, he recovered. This happened last winter. After this shooting, Zhao was always accompanied by several people when traveling between Shanghai and Changzhou, and the protection along the way was very thorough. For several months, everything was peaceful. Yesterday evening, around 9:00 PM, Zhao came to Shanghai from Changzhou on the night express train. After arriving, he first hired a car to Leyi Lou for a short rest. At 10:15 PM, he planned to return home to sleep. However, after walking only a few steps, in the drizzling rain, he suddenly encountered two enemies who seemed familiar. They said, "Brother Xilin, wait a moment, let me shoot you once." Then, they fired two shots. One hit his abdomen, severing his large intestine, and the other missed. Zhao immediately fell to the ground, unconscious. The thugs, seeing that their goal had been achieved, took the opportunity to escape without a trace. Afterwards, he was taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment by car. The doctor performed an abdominal examination and administered artificial resuscitation. He is currently still in critical condition.

It's Difficult to Be a Father

Shen Genmao, 22 years old, from Suzhou, lives at No. 53 Zhejiang Road and works as a barber. Shen Jinlong, the father of the deceased, testified that he was 65 years old and only had this one son. He set up the barber shop. That day, he asked him to work, but he refused, so he gave him some advice, and he went out alone and suddenly took poison. The body was handed over to his father, Shen Jinlong, to take back for burial.

Maid Dismissed and Doesn't Return Home 161

Freely Combines With Garment Store Employee

Openly Says It Was Consensual

Store Employee Sentenced to Three Years and Six Months

Jin Lin, a woman from Lu Xu, Suzhou, used to work as a maid at the Zhongxin Hotel on Hankou Road. Her daughter, Jin Sanbao, is only seventeen years old and quite beautiful. Last year, she was introduced to the Yang family at No. 56 Yian Lane, Wang Jingan Temple Road, as a maid. Opposite the back door of the Yang family, at No. 30, is the Dahua Garment Store. Zhao Changfu, an employee from Taixing, 24 years old, is a young and handsome bachelor. He became acquainted with Jin Girl when they saw each other coming and going. On the 8th of this month, the Yang family suddenly dismissed Jin Girl. Unexpectedly, Jin did not return to her mother's house, but went directly to find Zhao Changfu. They went to the New World Company rooftop garden to play. At 10:00 PM, tired of playing, this young couple, unable to control their emotions, went to room 45 of the Southeast Hotel on Baike Road and had intercourse for two nights. On the 10th, at 12:00 AM, they moved to room 24 of the Kade Hotel on Kade Road and continued to have intercourse for one night. However, after the Yang family dismissed Jin Girl, they sent someone to her mother's house the next day to ask if Jin Girl had returned. Her mother, Jin Lin, was still unaware and only then realized something was wrong. She went to Yian Lane to investigate. People said they saw Jin Girl go out to watch a play with Zhao Changfu, an employee of the garment store. The woman then reported to the Jingan Temple Police Station. Chinese detectives Cui Buyun and Qian Xianting arrested Zhao in the Dahua Garment Store. He confessed without denying it and said that Jin Girl was still in the Kade Hotel. The detectives went to arrest Jin Sanbao and brought them both back to the police station. The police chief ordered Zhao to be detained and Jin Girl to be temporarily sent to the Jiliang Institute for care. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang came forward to state the facts, saying that Jin Girl had been sent to Guangren Hospital by the police station for examination and it was confirmed that her hymen had been broken. Although the girl claimed to be seventeen years old, according to Chinese age reckoning, she may not be sixteen years old, so the age issue is relevant to the sentence and should be investigated. Jin Lin testified that she was 44 years old and her daughter Sanbao was 17 years old, born in the year of the Dragon, on the eighth day of the twelfth lunar month. She used to work as a maid in the Yang family. On the sixth of this month, the Yang family sent someone to her place to ask if Jin Girl had returned. She had not returned, so she went to Yian Lane to investigate and only then did she learn the truth. She reported it to the police station and now requests that the defendant be punished. Jin Sanbao testified that she had known the defendant since February of this year due to clothing manufacturing, but they had never had a relationship. On the recent Dragon Boat Festival, the employer dismissed her because she thought her clothes were too short. She wanted to go home, but her mother was very fierce and she was afraid of being punished, so she went to the New World Company to play with the defendant and the store owner's wife. At 10:00 PM, they went out and went to the Southeast Hotel to open a room. However, this was consensual and there was no coercion. Judge Feng Shide asked Jin Girl who had the idea to open a room and who initiated it. The girl answered that the defendant first said, "Let's go open a room, okay?" She answered, "Okay." So they stayed at the Southeast Hotel for two nights and later moved to the Kade Hotel for one night. This matter was voluntary. The defendant confessed to the adultery, but said that after leaving the New World Company, he advised her to go home, but the girl said that her mother was violent and did not want to go back and voluntarily borrowed a machine room. Finally, police lawyer Wang stated that according to the plaintiff's testimony, her age was actually not yet sixteen years old, so the defendant actually committed rape and should be investigated. Judge Feng sentenced the defendant Zhao Changfu to three years and six months of imprisonment for raping a girl under the age of sixteen. The number of days of detention before the judgment is final will be counted as two days equivalent to one day of imprisonment. The girl was taken back by her mother.

Enticement is Certainly a Crime

But the Young Girl Has No Sense of Shame

Wang Xiaosan Covets Abao

Abao Actually Agrees Immediately

Li Abao, a woman from Yangzhou, is twenty years old, of average appearance, and lives at No. 48 Weixing Lane, Tuopeng Road. She is a female worker at the Shenxin No. 7 Cotton Mill. Wang Xiaosan, a fellow villager, coveted Abao. On the afternoon of the 6th of this month, around 2:00 PM, he asked a friend named Ying Xizi to go to the house of Yangzhou woman Li Jiang (Abao's cousin), next door at No. 46, and conspired with Kong Qingsheng and Wang Changjin (also from Yangzhou) to lure Abao out. They hired a car at the Pingliang Road vegetable market, and Ying and Kong accompanied the girl to the Bund on Wuma Road, where Wang Xiaosan was waiting. Seeing that Li Abao had been tricked by the group, he was delighted to have his lover and praised the pimps for their skillful methods. However, Abao was afraid that Wang was a bad person and showed signs of timidity. Ying Xizi patted his chest to reassure her. The woman knew Ying. Wang Xiaosan and Abao took a car to a hotel in the French Concession for a night of adultery. The next day, they went to the Tangshan Hotel on Tangshan Road in the Public Concession to continue their joy. Since Abao's disappearance, her mother, Li Zhang, had been searching everywhere for her, but there was no news. The day before yesterday morning at 8:00 AM, a report was made to the Yulin Road Police Station, and detective Li Minglin found Li Abao on Dagu Road after an investigation. After learning the truth, he secretly went to arrest Li Jiang, Kong Qingsheng, Wang Changjin, and others. Wang Xiaosan, who lived at No. 2185 Dongyouheng Road, had heard the news and fled. Ying Xizi could not be arrested either. The police chief ordered the three defendants to be detained separately. Li Abao was taken back by her mother, Zhang. Yesterday morning, the police sent Li Jiang, Kong Qingsheng, and Wang Changjin to the First Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin described the facts in detail. The girl, Li Abao, wearing a blue Western-style cloth shirt, black silk trousers, stockings, and satin shoes, with short hair, lowered her head and spoke calmly. She said that her fiancé, a coppersmith, lived on Xiangyan Bridge and was allowed to marry by her mother. She briefly described the circumstances and said that the matter was entirely due to being fooled by Ying Xizi, who was on the run. At the time, her cousin, the defendant Li Jiang, called her out, saying she wanted to say a word, and she fell into their trap. Kong Qingsheng and Wang Changjin had both been to the hotel. When questioned, the three defendants Li Jiang and others gave evasive answers and asked for leniency. Judge Shen Bingrong ordered them to be remanded in custody separately for further review.

Wu Yuezhen Sues Husband for Abandonment 162

Demands Zhang Dehua Pay 8,000 Yuan

Wu Yuezhen, a young woman from Wuxian, Suzhou, lives with her mother in the Chengyu Lane on Lafayette Road in the French Concession. In June of last year, she married Zhang Dehua as a concubine. Recently, she was abandoned. She hired lawyer Chen Guocai to file a lawsuit with the Shanghai Local Court, stating that she was suing for the abandonment of a concubine. The plaintiff, a weak woman, relied on her mother for a living. In February of last year, Zhang Dehua suddenly met her and, with sweet words, she fell in love at first sight. The love affair began, and she became pregnant. In June, she officially married him as a concubine. They rented a house and bought furniture, and lived together. She thought the marriage was perfect and she could rely on him for the rest of her life. Unexpectedly, the defendant, a lecherous man, was tired of the old and loved the new. The former oath was still fresh, but his attitude had changed. He went out in search of pleasure and forgot to return. At first, she tried to be tolerant and did her best to endure it. But in January of this year, she gave birth to a daughter. But the defendant was heartless and had no pity. Not only did he ignore her, but he also suddenly cut off the plaintiff's regular expenses and asked someone to say that he wanted to divorce the concubine. The man was wicked to the extreme, leaving her miserable and heartbroken. Adding to her worries was the crying baby. Even if she wanted to remarry, how easy would it be? Unfortunately, her old mother died after she married. Helpless, without any means of support, she had to resign herself to her fate and endure her remaining years. She had previously applied for mediation, but it was unsuccessful. If this dragged on, both mother and daughter would be in danger of freezing and starving. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit according to the law to seek relief. The plaintiff's maintenance fee is calculated at 20 yuan per month for twenty years, totaling 4,800 yuan. The daughter's upbringing fee is calculated at 200 yuan per year for sixteen years, totaling 3,200 yuan. The two total 8,000 yuan, which should be paid by the defendant at once, so that she can deposit the money and live off the interest. She respectfully submits this complaint and requests that the court quickly summon the defendant to court for interrogation and judgment. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the hearing was held. The judge asked the plaintiff Wu Yuezhen her age and origin. Because the defendant Zhang Dehua did not appear, the judge announced that the hearing would be postponed to the next time.

Putuo is one of the four famous mountains in China. It faces the sea on all four sides, with beautiful scenery and magnificent temples, which are rare. Travelers come all year round. The Yousheng Travel Agency at the intersection of Niuzhuang Road and Laohai Road in this city is the only travel agency in Shanghai. It has specially chartered a Dahua ship to go directly to Putuo. It is scheduled to set sail at 3:00 PM on the 18th of this month and will arrive in Shanghai around 7:00 AM on the 20th, which is very time-saving. forward contracts. The market was particularly quiet afterward, with prices standing outside 24 taels. The day's overall situation is recorded below:

Yarn and Cotton 179

Yarn Market Selling Pressure Continues

New Low Prices Constantly Discovered

The cotton yarn market declined and then stabilized in the afternoon. However, real demand remained weak, and all parties had no hope for development. The overseas situation was still deteriorating, and the economic situation in all directions was extremely barren. People's livelihoods were increasingly difficult, so it was difficult for cotton yarn sales to improve. Most Zhuang customers from North China stationed in Shanghai closed down and returned home due to the lack of business, which shows the scarcity of business. Japanese factories were making efforts in all directions, and the sales of Chinese yarn were stolen by them. However, most people in the local area believe that the recent storm of price declines may have a slight rebound. However, the world cotton industry is still in a tragic situation.

Auction Prices Drop Another One or Two Taels: According to the opening of the market, the selling pressure in the market was strong, and the decline continued. Prices for each month fell by 1.2, 3, 4, and 7 qian. The afternoon opening situation was still weak, and new low prices were found in the second session. Later, profit-takers covered their short positions, and prices rebounded in each month, resulting in a flat outcome. The total transaction volume for the day was 33,700 bales. (Xiaoji Cotton) Sowing is completed. The climate is good. Cotton fields have increased by 15% compared to last year.

(Xiaoxi Cotton) Insufficient rainfall in several producing areas after sowing. But overall, the weather is smooth, and development is excellent. This year may have 80% of the harvest.

Free Talk

Diverse Discussions by Tan Shan

The Mentality of Island People 194

— Zhan Lu

The mentality of island people is becoming increasingly apparent to the world! Treating others' land as their lifeline is already ridiculous! What's especially ridiculous is that, while repeatedly claiming that others are unorganized countries, they consider countries that have a general assassinated with a bomb or a prime minister killed with a gun to be organized countries.

Narrow-mindedness, jealousy, and boasting are the three primary elements of the island people's mentality! Not only is this the mentality of the military, but it is also the mentality of their literati.

The complete works of the great poet Gao Qingqiu of the late Yuan and early Ming dynasties exist in a fine paper edition at the Aoki Sozan Hall in that country. The book is printed well! Unfortunately, it includes commentaries by Kondo Gensui of that country, adding dung to the Buddha's head, which I find deeply unfair to Qingqiu.

"Buying a thousand gold for a precious sword, the demon weeps for Taiyin, opening the box before the lamp, an infinite offering of your heart." This is Qingqiu's poem about swords. Because the precious sword of the Taishi country (i.e., Persia) is renowned throughout history, Qingqiu wrote, "Buying a thousand gold for a Taishi sword." Kondo Gensui, consumed by jealousy, added this marginal note: "Compared to a Japanese sword, it must have a difference between lead and iron."

"The deserted palace is filled with long moss at the end of spring, the skirt no longer sweeps the ground. I fear Xishi is a fairy, and there must be a pavilion in the cave." This is Qingqiu's poem about Xishi Cave, in which he compares Xishi Cave to a different world, not of this earth, which is the poet's ideal. Who knew that Mr. Kondo, consumed by jealousy, would add this marginal note: "The remains of a lewd woman, how could there be a different world?"

Five hundred years ago, the poet praised a Taishi sword! He had to say that the Taishi sword was lead, and the Japanese sword was iron. Only he could utter such an arbitrary statement. As for whether Xishi was a lewd woman, I fear everyone would deny it! Where exactly is the birthplace of lewd women? I would like to ask people from China and abroad for a fair critique! It is unlikely to be the Wu and Yue kingdoms two or three thousand years ago.

The Problem of Bribery 195

— Tao Zaidong

The newspaper reports on the draft articles of the law on punishing corruption. Any civil servant who receives bribes or illegal benefits of more than one thousand yuan will be sentenced to death. Requesting promises or receiving bribes of more than five hundred yuan but less than one thousand yuan will be sentenced to life imprisonment. Furthermore, if a civil servant commits a crime under this article, the proposed bribe or benefit will be confiscated. If all or part cannot be confiscated, its value will be recovered, etc. This is a special law, different from the ordinary law, i.e., the criminal law, and is a special provision for calculating the amount of stolen goods and sentencing accordingly. The intention is to severely punish corruption and the law emphasizes calculating the amount of stolen goods. However, prison situations are ever-changing, and abstract legislation is difficult to be comprehensive. Suppose that someone, Mr. A, offers his wife, daughter, or sister to a civil servant as a gift. The civil servant accepts and, as requested, illegally appoints him to a position or unfairly judges a lawsuit in his favor. If the matter is discovered and reported to the authorities, and the investigation proves it to be true, he will be brought before a special court. Whether a woman is a bribe and whether her beauty and talent are benefits is worthy of research. In this case, the cause of the civil servant's crime is clearly this woman. If she is not considered a bribe, then the anti-corruption law does not apply, and even the criminal law would not consider it a crime of bribery. He may be punished for dereliction of duty or face administrative disciplinary action, which is clearly a case of a severe crime receiving a light punishment. Compared to those sentenced to death for one thousand yuan and those permanently banned for five hundred yuan, the national laws are inevitably biased. If she is considered a bribe, then the essence of this law lies in calculating the amount of stolen goods. This woman is neither a slave under Tang law, akin to cattle and horses, nor a common prostitute with a fixed price. Therefore, the method of calculating the amount of stolen goods is exhausted, and there is no way to confiscate or recover the value. The essence of this law in calculating the amount of stolen goods lies in the thousand yuan. Whether one is above or below the thousand yuan mark is a matter of life and death. I have pondered it a hundred times.

World Snippets 196

Mrs. Helen Wills Moody, a famous American tennis queen, is also a perennial champion in the international tennis world. She has repeatedly retained her titles. She recently went to Europe to participate in a major competition, bringing with her twenty-four tennis rackets, which she cherishes as her treasures.

Gare St. Lazare, a famous French railway station, is the most well-equipped railway station. Passengers can buy clothes, books, and all kinds of food and drinks. There are also dentists who can treat teeth, and barbers who can give haircuts or shaves. There are also long-distance telephones that people can use to contact relatives and friends in distant places about important matters. There is also a cinema where people can watch movies to pass the time while their cars are being repaired. When the train is about to arrive, the screen will automatically announce it so that passengers can prepare to board.

In 1931, not a single criminal was executed in Scotland. There were also absolutely no executions in prisons.

Last year, a particularly unusual item was left unclaimed at the London railway station lost and found office: a baby. The station staff found it in the waiting room. (Hai Ke)

If one gains something, one should suffer a loss. I sincerely wish to learn from legal experts. Please do not regard this as a fictitious question. In the pursuit of wealth and power, base behaviors are inevitable. Since the late Qing Dynasty, as far as I have seen and heard, there have indeed been such things. Moreover, when I was working in the Ministry of Justice during the Guangxu and Xuantong eras, there was such a fact in a case of accepting bribery assigned by the emperor. The case involved several crimes, and the original charge included a certain crime. According to the Qing law, the heavier punishment was applied, and the lighter crime was not considered. Therefore, the confession prepared in the initial draft of the indictment, which is now the section describing the facts in the judgment, could be briefly mentioned. However, this is not in accordance with the laws of the Republic of China, nor is it in accordance with the special law on punishing corruption. Therefore, I presumptuously advocate that there is a need to supplement the draft law with three points: A. The term "bribe" in this law is not limited to property. B. Bribes that cannot be valued should be punished according to criminal law, and those with serious circumstances should be punished more severely, even up to the death penalty. C. For stolen goods that cannot be compensated, appropriate punishment may be imposed. With such supplements, the previous questions can be resolved. However, there are still doubts. It may be possible to apply this to an unknowing woman, but if the woman knows the situation, she is an accomplice. Moreover, there are many cases where women scheme for men, and the idea originates from the woman, making her the instigator of the crime. What is even more difficult is when the man is unaware. Suppose that A and B commit a criminal offense or are subject to disciplinary action. While in custody, A's wife or daughter, using B's name, offers herself to the civil servant as a gift. The civil servant accepts and illegally declares B innocent or dismisses the charges. In such a case, there is a bribe and a recipient of the bribe, but no briber, and the law is at an end. Generally speaking, laws are like bags, and facts are like awls. When an awl is placed in a bag, its point will immediately be seen, or it will emerge completely. It is almost impossible to encompass everything. What should those responsible for legislation do? Mr. Zaidong has long served as a legal official and has held positions in societies. He has both legal knowledge and experience. This issue is related to legislation and is not just an interesting article. It has practical value. If there are experts in the country who can provide answers, it is what my friend hopes for and what this publication welcomes. However, the space is limited, and the text should not be too long. Ju Jian's note.

Old Customs of the Dragon Boat Festival in Suzhou 197

— Sun Choucheng

According to Suzhou customs, every family hangs calamus swords on their doors during the Dragon Boat Festival. They all drink realgar wine for lunch, and children write the character "king" on their foreheads with realgar. The room is filled with burning Atractylodes lancea and Angelica dahurica to ward off epidemics. Although the government promotes the national calendar and abolishes the Dragon Boat Festival, the people still adhere to their habits and continue to celebrate it. This year, because the Japanese invaded and the 19th Route Army retreated to the second line of defense, families above the middle class inside and outside the city evacuated. Now, having returned to Suzhou after the disaster, I feel especially happy. Therefore, the crowding of the small food markets on that day was inversely proportional to the lack of interest in the food displayed three months ago. Except for party and government organs and schools of all sizes, which were restricted by the ban and continued to work and hold classes as usual, other industrial and commercial sectors took advantage of the holiday to rest. Men in red and women in green flocked to the streets, causing traffic jams. All the entertainment venues inside and outside the city tripled their profits. Huang Maoquan, the first regiment commander of the 119th brigade of the 60th division of the 19th Route Army stationed in Suzhou, witnessed this situation and marveled at the rare sight.

On Thrift and Frugality to Save the Country (10) 198

— Narrated by Nie Zengjifen, Written by Son Qijie

Gu Tinglin said, "The rise and fall of a nation is the responsibility of every man." I would say, "It is especially the responsibility of every woman." Rejecting extravagant clothing, accessories, and utensils, and being diligent and thrifty to encourage men will create a good social atmosphere, cultivate the nation's vitality, and ensure world peace. Is this not the responsibility of us women? I hope that my fellow women will not dismiss this as a cliché.

Appendix 1: Recently, I read "The Handbook for Getting Rich" written by Western doctor Wang Licai, which describes the story of his great-great-grandmother, Zhang Taiyi, who was known for her chastity and filial piety. She spun twelve taels of yarn every day, earning fifty copper coins. After providing food for her aunt, two children, and herself, she was still able to save money to pay off her debts. Note: Two hundred years ago, prices were low. With one copper coin, one could buy a bowl of sauce, vinegar, oil, and wine at a sauce shop, which was called "four bowls for one coin." The price of white rice was only two coins per liter. See Lu Jiaoshu's story by Qi Fan Niu. Jie comments: The story of Zhang Yi's chastity and filial piety began in the 29th year of the Qianlong era. At that time, the price of rice was already fifty coins per liter. Ordinary people could only spin six or seven taels of yarn per day, so the average daily income was only twenty or thirty coins. Therefore, the price of rice was about ten coins per liter. Emperor Gaozong made three tours of the south of the Yangtze River and liked to be extravagant, which cost the local people a lot of money. Social customs gradually became extravagant, and prices rose accordingly. Lu Jiaoshu's story took place during the Kangxi era, which proves the effectiveness of Emperor Shengzu's practice of thrift and frugality. However, two coins per liter of white rice refers to the extremely low price. According to Zhang Wenduan Cong Xun Zhai's words written in the 36th year of the Kangxi era, at that time, white rice cost four qian of silver per stone, which was only about four or five coins per liter. The land tax was low, and there were no taxes on other daily necessities. Moreover, farmers were able to work in peace, and industry and commerce were not engaged in luxury goods. This allowed agricultural products to increase, so prices were low, and farmers and merchants could still make a profit. At the end of the Ming Dynasty, prices were high, and people's lives were difficult. However, it only took twenty or thirty years to lower prices to this level, which shows the close relationship between prices and politics. Low prices make life easier and people happier. High prices make life difficult and people think of rebellion. Therefore, those who cannot make prices low and life easy are said to have bad politics. In other words, it is a failure to practice the Three People's Principles.

Therefore, he also led his troops to march through the streets in formation and held a full-group dinner at the Wang Feiji Public Sports Field in the city to observe the customs and enjoy the festivities. Although the dishes were not very exquisite, they were all exceptionally clean. The raising of cups and chopsticks was all done according to commands. The actions were uniform, and officers and soldiers enjoyed themselves together. The audience praised their strict military discipline and close-knit spirit. After the meal, they were led to the park for sightseeing. The strangest thing was that the people of Wu were timid and afraid of soldiers. Whenever they encountered soldiers, they would call them "gray camels" or "old soldiers" and avoid them from afar, afraid to interact with them. Unexpectedly, the actions of the tourists in the park on that day were completely different from usual. Not only did young men rush to talk with the soldiers about the anti-Japanese war in Shanghai, but even women and children approached the gun racks to examine the enemy's guns and cannons and admire the globally renowned bamboo hats. It showed that people regarded the soldiers of the 19th Route Army as fighting for national dignity and eliminating the great scourge for the people, and that they were truly the pillars of the country, unlike other military men who preyed on the people. When the regiment marched, in addition to using military music as a guide, it also used Cantonese gongs and drums, which was very lively. Therefore, the audience was as thick as a wall. Affection and aversion arise from the inherent nature of the people and cannot be forced by power. It is said that one convinces people with virtue, which is heartfelt and sincere. Seeing the attitude of the people of Wu towards the 19th Route Army, I am all the more convinced. I hope that those who wear tiger amulets in the country will take this as a warning and reorganize their troops so that the guns are aimed outward.

Talking about Pleasure Boats on the Qinhuai River 199

— Bao Zheng

Jinling is originally a scenic spot of the Six Dynasties. Since the government established its capital here, the market has become prosperous. The area around the Confucius Temple is lined with tea houses, and singing and music never cease. Every summer, pleasure boats on the Qinhuai River, following a long-standing tradition, also appear in season, no longer as desolate and lonely as before. Pleasure boats are divided into three types: large, medium, and small. The equipment inside the boats is all-encompassing. The prices vary depending on the time and needs. Once it is past dinner time, the banks of the Qinhuai River are filled with people, and the pleasure boats are as numerous as ants. In the sound of oars, the singing of orioles and the chirping of swallows can be faintly heard. The sounds of banter are everywhere. Most of these people are staff members of various agencies. They feel quite bored after work, so they gather two or three friends and flock to the pleasure boats, either to call prostitutes to drink wine or to brew tea to entertain guests. They talk about the past and the present, endlessly. Or they lie on the couch or take a nap on the veranda, looking up at the vastness of the universe and observing the prosperity of all things. At this time, the breeze is gentle, and the ripples are calm. They are carefree and happy. I, the reporter, briefly record this to tell the readers.

The theatre has always shown foreign films, and this is the first time it has premiered a domestic film.

A Tale of Two Habitats or Horses (78) 201

— The Master of Seeking Happiness

Chapter 10: Powerful Figures Abuse Their Authority, Relying on Kind Women for Comfort; Take the Short Route, Offer Bribes for Personal Gain, Generals Recruit Mountain Bandits

Let's talk about An Yutian sitting quietly in the reception room of the Aide-de-Camp Office in the military governor's headquarters, waiting for instructions. He had been sitting and waiting from one o'clock in the afternoon until after five o'clock. The aide-de-camp had not yet summoned him to go up to see Governor Ye, nor had he informed him that he would not be seen. He was just sitting there in the chair like a wooden statue, unable to move or walk. He was secretly complaining, fearing that he would turn into a petrified stone. Finally, he saw that many lucky people had been seen by the governor and left. The sky was gradually darkening, and no new people were coming in to sit down. Only about ten or so guests were left in the outer reception room, still waiting with gloomy faces like mud sculptures, hoping for news that was like a stone sinking into the sea. After all, he was young and energetic, unlike those old gentlemen in the next seats who had such deep cultivation. For a moment, he couldn't bear the hunger, thirst, and fatigue, and couldn't suppress his anxiety and resentment. He waited for the aide-de-camp to pass by him and suddenly stood up to stop him, wrinkling his brow and trembling his voice, he lowered his head and gently asked, "Excuse me, may I ask, did you pass my name card up? Will I be seen? Has the governor given any instructions?" The aide-de-camp moved a bundle of name cards to the side of the table, became furious, glared at him, raised his eyebrows, and spoke to him, "My dear sir, how can you ask me such a thing? How would I know? It is true that I eat the marshal's rice. Marshal Bai specially sent me to serve you gentlemen. I have to sit here for you gentlemen, and take out the name cards and say that you have official business to see the marshal. I have to run my legs off to report to the marshal one by one for you gentlemen. I don't have the guts to not pass your name card up. As for the marshal, he is very busy with official business and has many meetings. If everyone had to be seen as soon as they arrived, how could that be possible? We just have to compile a list of these name cards and send it to the marshal to look over. He will summon whoever he wants to see first. When he mentions someone, we will come down and announce it. We are just following orders and cannot make decisions on our own. Before he has spoken, how would I know if he will see you or not? Am I a worm in his stomach?" An Yutian was scolded and his face turned red from ear to ear. He was almost so embarrassed that he had nowhere to put his face. But he still endured his anger and said awkwardly, "Don't blame me, don't blame me, I have been waiting too long. I want to ask you to go up and ask again. If it can be done, it can be done. If it can't be done, then forget it. Why do you have to get so angry?"

Shen Bao Local Supplement, Republic of China, Year 21, June 14, Tuesday

(No Additional Cost)

Commentary

Opium Public Sale 202

— Buddha

Yesterday, the Japanese newspaper "Mainichi Shimbun" reported that Song is trying to implement the opium public sale again this time, after the proposal for public sale failed last year. His confidants Zhang Shouyong and Tang Haian are trying to carry out the public sale plan according to the plan set last year. If this is indeed the case, I have a few more words to say.

Everyone can talk about the harm opium does to the country and its people, so there is no need for me to say it again. However, there are special clauses in the law prohibiting opium, but private planting, transportation, and consumption have not disappeared. Moreover, some provinces have special tax offices, and some provinces force opium planting. Opium has always been an open secret. Now it is simply open, without having to hide it. That is not necessarily impossible.

However, since the country has issued a strict prohibition order, private planting, consumption, and transportation are still somewhat taboo and inconvenient. If it is made public, it will inevitably have a promotional nature. The number of smokers will inevitably increase suddenly. Originally, some people said that our country has become a "bandit" country. The explanation is that it refers to opium and bandits. If it is made public again, what kind of country will the country become? What kind of people will the people become?

If it is done for the sake of national income, and endured with pain, then there are many more nationalized businesses that can be done. For example, prostitution can also be made public, and gambling can be specially taxed. Once promoted, the effect will be huge. In this way, it will become a country of "bandits, gamblers, and prostitutes." Please close your eyes and think about what kind of phenomenon it will become. It will make our Republic of China forever sink into the abyss, with no daylight to be seen.

Of course, if the government really has this determination to promote it, then the previous failure due to poor planning will be remedied with a better plan. I can only optimistically hope for success and celebrate the happiness of the country's future.

Cicada-wing arms and lotus-root limbs reveal jade-like skin, short hair like crow's silk, curly and fluffy, most soul-stirring is the truly exquisite place, where the high peaks of the breasts are hidden.

Evening makeup just finished, like the red of the setting sun, tenderly calling her love with a smile, feeling lazy at the dance hall tonight, she goes for a drive on Yuyuan Road.

Dense buildings like a caged pigeon coop, the surrounding walls do not allow wind to pass through, children cry and girls weep, noisy, lighting an oil lamp to catch bedbugs.

Science

The Principles of Photography 204

— Gao Qian

The use of photography is very broad, and it is used in science, military affairs, law, and art. The various techniques involved contain extremely profound theories, which cannot be explained in a few words. I will now explain the principles of common procedures as follows:

(1) Focusing: Before taking a photo, it is necessary to focus on the ground glass. Because the image has a certain focal point, the ground glass must be placed precisely at the focal point to make the image clear. Focusing is aligning the focal point to make the image very clear.

(2) Photography: After focusing, a dry plate holder can be installed for photography. When photographing, the lens is opened to allow light to shine on the dry plate.

The dry plate is coated with a compound like silver bromide, which changes when exposed to light.

(3) Developing: Although the emulsion on the dry plate changes, it is invisible to the eye. To turn the image into a black shadow, it must undergo the action of a chemical solution.

The developing solution is a chemical reducing agent. When the dry plate is immersed in the developing solution, the silver bromide that has been exposed to light is reduced to silver particles, revealing the black shadow of the scene. White objects reflect light strongly, so more silver particles are reduced. The white clothes we wear appear as dark black images on the dry plate. Black objects, such as hair, reflect very little light, so the dry plate changes little, and the image becomes blank.

(4) Fixing: Although the image has been developed, the dry plate cannot be exposed to white light, otherwise the image will turn completely black. The developed dry plate must be immersed in a fixing solution to dissolve all the unexposed silver bromide. Then, only the black image remains on the negative. After washing and drying, it becomes the "negative" seen in photography.

(5) Printing: The image on the negative is the opposite of the real object. White clothes are black, and black hair is blank. Therefore, a printing process is required to obtain an image that is the same as the real object. Printing involves placing a photosensitive paper under the negative and exposing it to light. The hair area is blank on the negative, so more light passes through. White clothes are black on the negative, so less light passes through. Following the principle of developing, we process the photosensitive paper in developing and fixing solutions to obtain a "positive image" that is the same as the real object.

The number of people in our country who know how to take photos is increasing every day, but all the raw materials and equipment used are foreign products. The amount of money flowing out every year is certainly not small. Now, Chinese people can manufacture photosensitive paper, and some simple equipment can also be made domestically. However, the most important "dry plates" and "cameras" have not been touched at all. The Japanese have long been able to make their own "dry plates." It is hoped that photography enthusiasts in our country will pay more attention to this.

Learning to Write and Draw

Chinese Language Class 205

— Ying Dai

Clang, clang, clang! The Chinese language class at C School's D classroom has begun. An old gentleman wearing a pair of "horse's foot" glasses nervously walks onto the stage. When he calls the roll, all the students in the grade should be present, but after he finishes calling the roll and looks up, one-third of the students have already slipped out through the side door. He happily lectures on the platform, but the students below continue to slip away one by one. In the end, only five or six students remain out of dozens. Although they play this farce every Chinese language class, this time, because too many students left, it could not escape the notice of the old gentleman with dull eyes. He noticed the students slipping away and began to interrogate the remaining few, but they all refused to tell him. His pent-up anger suddenly flared up, and he slammed the desk, dropped the book, and shouted the old tune of "national slaves." He went to the academic affairs office to report to the principal, but the next day, the principal did not express anything.

The third day, the old gentleman came to teach Chinese language class, and the students continued to slip away one after another.

Chinese students' dislike of studying Chinese has long become a very common thing. Here, I am reminded of a joke from my student days. The year we graduated, there were a total of twenty-two students in the class. On the day of the Chinese composition exam, some of the students did not know how to write, and they were extremely anxious. Finally, one student wrote seven compositions for them. I also wrote three compositions for them. But the joke happened because, in three hours, it was impossible to write several good compositions. I used a pencil to write a draft for them and passed it on as a perfunctory task. Who knew that the friend sitting in front of me transcribed many of the cursive characters on my draft paper incorrectly. As a result, after submitting the paper, the teacher noticed it and marked it as a failure. He did not receive a high school diploma because of this, even after six years of hard work. At first, I wholeheartedly wanted to help him, but in the end, I harmed him. This matter has left me feeling somewhat sad to this day. But here, we can also see the general Chinese proficiency of middle school students. Not to mention writing, they can even copy incorrectly. The reason is that they usually dislike Chinese language class and are unwilling to write compositions.

Business Acumen

Four Screws 206

— Wu Wei

Once, I went to a barber shop for a haircut. About a quarter of an hour after I sat down, another customer came in. I heard Xiao Sanzi, who was cutting my hair, say, "Four screws." At the same time, a barber reluctantly went up to cut the customer's hair.

I heard the phrase "four screws" and saw the barber's extremely unhappy expression. I knew that the phrase must be their secret code and that it must be related to that customer. So, I wanted to ask them, but I didn't. Later, I saw that the customer's haircut and shave were finished before mine. So, I couldn't help but ask Xiao Sanzi, "What does 'four screws' mean?" I said, "Oh, that means four 'eight-open' (referring to eight 5-cent coins)."

"You said that phrase was probably related to that customer."

"Yes, that guy always only gives four 'eight-open.' I've cut his hair twice, and he always gives so little. So, I told them not to waste their effort."

"You're being too unfair. Four 'eight-open' is already the price you set," I said, as if defending the customer.

"It's not wrong, sir, but we always hope that customers will give a little more so that we can earn more when we split the earnings."

Hearing this, I secretly said "shame." Fortunately, I have always given them six "eight-open," otherwise, I would probably hear the call of "four screws" next time I came in, or even see their extremely unhappy expressions.

Family Problems

The Burden of Men 207

— Wu Wei

Shanghai is a prosperous metropolis and one of the world's largest commercial centers. Nanjing Road is the most bustling place in all of Shanghai. The shop windows are always filled with cosmetics, consumer goods,

fabrics, such as modern silk, georgette, and jersey, etc., especially supplies for women. It is almost impossible to find a store that specializes in men's supplies, which shows that women's extravagance is even greater than men's. Because the more of these stores there are, the higher the degree of women's extravagance is shown. The establishment of these stores is, of course, due to demand, but at the same time, men's burdens have also increased.

My old classmate S earns a monthly salary of 120 yuan. Normally, maintaining a small family would be more than enough. However, he told me that he always felt that it was not enough because his wife alone spends 80 to 90 yuan a month. Her expenses include silk stockings costing several yuan each, two or three pairs a month; perfume (White Rose) at least one bottle a month; leather shoes one pair a month (at the very least); cigarettes (Five Flowers brand) ten dimes a month; and fabrics and face powder. She alone spends half of his salary each month. I heard that S's wife is an extremely modern woman. She thinks that it is nothing for a woman to spend this much. But, alas! In today's society, it is probably not easy for a man to bear so much.

Fu Gui 208

Dear Mr. Jianhua,

I am writing to express my admiration for your ambition in industry. I have investigated and found that erasers are not yet made in China, but this is a commonly used item that is bought in small quantities at high prices. If we add up the amount used nationwide, a large amount of money flows out of the country. I am also impressed by your ambition to engage in manufacturing and recover these profits. However, I have no research on rubber manufacturing. I will answer your inquiries to the best of my knowledge as follows: (1) It is not very suitable for small-scale home industry manufacturing. (2) The amount of money needed to open a factory depends on the size of the factory and is related to various issues such as the size of the machines, location, and labor costs. It is difficult to estimate accurately. At a minimum, at least 7,000 to 8,000 yuan would be needed. (3) The chemical formula for rubber is CioHi6, which is a hydrogen-carbon substance. Its analyzed composition should be published in a separate scientific article. The above is a brief reply. Because I am still studying and do not have much free time, the letter is not very detailed. I apologize for this.

Sincerely,

Li Naizheng

June 9th

(Mailing address: 565 Meibaige Road)
